O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, very dear sons, I have completed this book which is the end of the knowledge of medicine along with its contents, and I have finished it through its explanations and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in vision that I would complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is completely unknown everywhere, so the science has perished and been lost, and nothing remains from it except the small descriptions in books by the ancients that hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed off and true knowledge is estranged.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I will revive it along with the ordering of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come along with the forms of surgical instruments of cautery and other tools of work with the adjustment of the declaration and preparation for them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good masters of hands in our time, the art of medicine has been estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for someone who undertakes this to ascend to the science of anatomy, as Galien says, so long as he knows the justice of members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of them, and their arrangement and moving and resting veins, and from where their origin is.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this Hippocrates says that the name with its name is much, and with its work is little, and similarly in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We warn you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above should guard himself lest he fall into error and harm people; thus I have often warned many who undertake this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish physician who cut, that is to say, an abscess of scrofula or the nape of a woman's neck, and cut the arteries of the neck; why then so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another physician who treated an ulcer of an elderly man's leg, and the ulcer was large; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the state of the sick person and the size of the ulcer, and I knew that if they were to cut it out, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another physician who undertook to treat the leg of a duke from our land, which was broken and had an open wound; and the ignorant doctor applied splints to the break over the wound by force, and did not leave any space for antiseptic treatment, and thus left it in that state until the leg became completely infected and gangrenous, and came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and relieve the leg; and when I removed the splints, he was at peace and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in every way the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the entire member was lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another physician who drained a suppurating abscess, and then inflamed it further through the wickedness of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For an ulcer, when it is pure of melancholic humor, it does not seem fitting that one touch it with iron unless it is in such a place where one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of one's hands is divided into two divisions: namely, a work where there is danger in multiple dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Why do you need to keep them safe so that the foolish gazer cannot speak evil of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Take your arms in custody, and begin your treatments lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you may come to salvation and be praised; and leave frightful diseases with miserable health; and take away from you what makes you doubt, and have courage within yourself so that you can come out of this world into the other one full of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on the treatment of a bad disease unless you are called a foolish doctor."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauterizing with fire and medicine poultices, and it is the chapter ordered from head to foot; and the forms of the instruments, and the handles of the cauterizer, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the application of leeches and wounds, and the removal of splinters and similar things; and it is the chapter ordered with the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is ordered from head to foot, with the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	So that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to tell the quality of the help and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the help and the harm is the longest word and most subtle science and secret response; and many wise people have spoken about this, and they agreed with each other; and I was not given much time to speak, because I fear the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterizing helps universally in all constitutions where there is material, except for two constitutions: namely, the hot constitution with material, and the dry constitution with material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the hot and dry constitution with material, some people said that cauterizing is great help, while others said the opposite: that cauterizing is not worth it for illnesses that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be cured with heat or dryness itself; and those who said the opposite said that cauterizing makes great help for hot and dry illnesses that come into men's bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man to its moisture in the constitution of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true at times through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, one should not meddle with it except for those who have tested it and know through long experience the chapter of cauterizing, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and cures and the pace of time; as for other complexions, we are not afraid of them, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors gathered together and agreed on cauterizing.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, son, that cauterizing with fire is a secret of the cure, and of greater goodness than cauterizing with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not harm except the member that is burned, and it does not hurt another member if you know its name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	The burning medicines spread from one member to another and bring grievous and difficult-to-cure diseases to the afflicted member, and perhaps kill the sick person.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire, because of its purity and goodness of its substance, does not do these things, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this to be true through experience and the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is in agreement with the truth of things. And for these reasons, I excuse myself from the length of my words, because I do not want to take away the secret which is answered by fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating it; accept this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on what time the cauterizations should be done, and appointed assistants.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable at any time, because the damage caused by them happens below and is removed by the aid of the cauterization; and indeed if the cauterizations are for necessary and urgent pains that cannot wait for the time when greater evil will come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think about it, dear son, as foolish people do; for the disease that is healed by cauterization does not have a relapse; and they say so themselves; but it is not so as they believe, because cauterizations are not just medicine that moves the complexion, and dries up the humors that cause the pain, and counts more than medicine in its speed of value, and in the virtue of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the sick person and the place of the disease and its virtue; and excesses are gathered in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered at a place where there is little excess and moisture, such as cauterizations of dens for pain, and the like things; and that kind of pain does not come back again; but it happens sometimes.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that cauterization is worth after medicine, but their intentions are false, and cauterization is considered the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in any disease and they do not work, then we administer the cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore it is clearly seen that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterizations made with a gold instrument are more effective than those made with iron, and they did not say this only because of the quality of gold and its high substance; and they said that the place of cauterization does not cause corruption, but that is not true because I have tried it and found that in some people it is true; and a gold cauterization is more effective than an iron one, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And besides, when you heat an iron instrument made of gold, you cannot tell if it is hot enough just by looking at the color of the gold, and it cools down immediately; and if it is heated too much, it becomes brittle; and thus there are many hindrances.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And therefore we use iron cauterizations because they have been made more convenient to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter from the head to the foot so that the view is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauteries are used for moist and cold on the brain, and there are two which are done because of an illness called "soda", and due to many humors that descend from the head towards themselves, and towards the ears, and for a multitude of dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and similarly to all illnesses that come from coldness such as paralysis and dropsy and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged by a dissolving medicine, cleansing the head three or four times, depending on what virtue and age and custom of the patient can endure; and then reapply the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on the scales; after that place the root of your palm over the root of his navel between his two eyes; and let blood come from the middle vein, then heat the cautery called "olivare", which is in this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the marked spot with ink, and move your hand slowly and evenly in a circular motion; then lift your hand suddenly, and reward the spot if you see the bone 1 small span's length; and if you don't see it, redo the cautery until you see the bone as I told you; after that take 1 spoonful of silk, moisten and soften cotton with it, and place it on the spot, and let it stay for 3 days; then put a wet linen compress in a burrow; and leave it on until the heat is gone; after that treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmacium" until it's healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old man said that the longer and more open the wound is, the more it purges itself; and for this reason it is beneficial.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And one of them said that the cautery should be left in place until part of the bone is charred, and then remove what has been burned off from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And the other one said that the cautery should be left in place until it is pressed so hard against the bone that an area as wide as a spindle (used by women to spin thread) is charred, so that the humors can flow out; and the wound should be left open for a long time; after that it should be treated and cooked.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And I think that both of these methods of cauterization are not good in all cases, except perhaps in people with a clear sign of fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them alone, because the flesh is weakened by continued natural solutions, as we have seen in other members; and similarly, when the patient's flesh is naturally weak and the first appearance of cauterization is more serious and painful for me, and with this I work towards a similar recovery.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	It seems we've reached the end of the text! The final phrase "de l'anciainne dolor du chief" can be translated to "from the old man's headache" or more literally, "from the ancient pain of the head". It appears to be a concluding remark or a note on the topic of cauterization, possibly written in an older style or from a historical perspective.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the headache is chronic and lasts long, the patient should use herbal remedies and pills called "cochie", and treatments for purging the head, and oils and plasters. And if one makes a cauterization as we have previously mentioned, it will not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's shoulder is of strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterize underneath it with the fire cautery a little as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Afterwards cauterize the tip of each horn of the head up to the bone, just as we have said before, and cauterize one in the place which is called "vasselz"; and it is one place where you put cupping glasses; and hold your hand so that you do not see even up to the bone: the patient feels much more great pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it later; and it is necessary that the horns' cauterizers be more subtle than those with which we cauterize the middle part of the head, and it is its shape:
dou cautere dou chief	from the head's cautery
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in some part of the head sudden pain comes and the eye is diseased up to the eyelid and the patient's shoulder has been purged by common medicines, and one has done all the other cures that I said in the division of diseases, and none of these things benefit: then he makes cauterizers according to two manners, that is to say with medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicine cauterizer is done thus: you take a spoonful of aloes, remove the rind and recopy it into one pot for two shoulders, then place the temple where the pain holds in such a way that you can put back the spoonful of aloes under the skin; and when it has been reapplied tie it well and leave it thus for 12 hours; and then untie it and scrape out the aloes' residue, and let the wound remain thus for two or three days; then apply on a poultice made from butter as long as pus comes.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the ointment treatment is finished, as long as it has been cured; and if you see fit to make those of some purging medicines that I have written or to treat with purging remedies.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The fire cauterizer is done thus: Heat the cauterizer in a brazier, and here is its shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is shaped like a clove or a small bundle of herbs; and in the middle there is a slight appearance; and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and twist the fire slightly, until the moisture of the pus is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is outside, and discharge an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Then place cotton in the shape of a sail, and put it on the painful area for three days; then I put moistened cotton in the wax, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this headache with a cautery called "cultellare", to the entire point, and be careful not to touch the artery in this headache which is not an old one.
de emigraine	the headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat the headache as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cauterization from medicine and iron does not help it, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and then sign it on the painful area with a line of half a finger's length, and lift your hand once, and do not touch the artery so that it burns just to the bone; and be careful of the jaw which moves when eating, and do not let the nerves have regard for the jaw and spasms come to the sick person, and be careful of the discharge of blood from the artery when it is touched, or if it has great fear and especially for one who does not know himself and is not experienced in studying; and leave the work to myself; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it hurts in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cauterization does not help the disease, and the sick person is suffering, then cauterize a second time in the same place on the head, as we have said before; and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Of the pain of the ears due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain comes to the ear due to coldness, and one has worked with dissolving medicines and other treatments that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then warm this spot called "point", which is its shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After point the entire area around the ailing ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move away a little above the root of the ear after you have marked the place where it hurts; and have 10 points around each ear; afterwards cure the spot until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be cured by cauterization is none other than those that move from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of disease; and do not make a cauterization for the semblances that come from heat and spasm of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this semblance of torture that moves from phlegm and purgations of the head and gargarism, and it does not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize the ailing area with 3 cauters: one at the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third in the joining of the two lips; and put the cauter on the part that appears to be healthy, and make the cauter hot near the corner of the head, above a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as one finger; and leave the cauter so high that the middle of the wound is burned. And this is the shape of the cauter:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And this is the shape of the cauter we put before, but it is a little more subtle and needs to be a little thicker; after that, cure the spot as I said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you cure it in the same way as we said before, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then make 4 cauters: 2 on the 2 horns of the head, and 1 in the middle of the head, and 1 on the spot that is called "vasselz" as we said before, and the last cauter on the mouth of the stomach; and cure it in the same way as we said before.
de litargie	De litargie.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	Give the patient large doses of herbs and purging pills to clear the head; after, rinse the patient's head thoroughly, and apply a mustard plaster on the back of the head as described in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method for cauterizing: do it just as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is well done like this, then the patient will be good; and if not, make three cauterizations on the head below the neck, with a space of two large pieces between each one, and treat it just as the others, and if you see that it is inflamed, and the patient is suffering, make one cauterization in the middle; and if necessary, two more above the two horns, and treat it until it is healed; and this cauterization which is called "olivare" as I said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with herbs and what we have said before; then rinse the patient's head, then make a cauterization in the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three above the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, make four cauterizations above the spine of the back; and leave it until the greatest part of the boil is burned, and lift your hand; then treat it until it is healed, and this is the cauterization which is called "olivare" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Epileptics should not use cauterization unless they are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first purify the brain with herbs and other remedies that we have mentioned in the section on treating severe and suffering patients with strong medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, make them gargle and chew on purifying substances that often include good meats; then rinse their head with water, and I will make one cauterization according to what we have said before, and one cauterization on the forehead, and on each horn; and if the patient is severe and suffering, make cauterizations as I have said to someone who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and this be the olive oil cauterization according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make one subtle cauterization in this way:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy the superfluities or moisture is corrupted and becomes thick phlegm, then make many cauterizations as we have said to someone who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the superfluities are declining towards melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then give them to drink something by which the brain may be purified, according to what was said before in the section on purifying the brain.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After rinsing the patient's head; then make one cloth of flax well made, also like a circle, which he puts inside his head; and the patient is to be cross-legged, and held firmly from all sides. Then present the poultice, and it must be moistened with old thyme balm; and the cauldron should be heated moderately, so that the liquid can be borne by the patient. Then empty the circle inside his head, and let it cool down. And do this to the patient once a week for as long as he is sick.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	Or, if you wish to cauterize the brain by making many small points around the entire cauterization. This method of cauterizing moistens the brain equally well; and then put on damp cotton soaked in balm and goose grease.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' affliction (possibly referring to eye problems or vision issues)
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When affliction comes to the eyes first by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and give the patient something to drink that purifies the head, and removes all moisture from it; and make them sweat or take a bath several times fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that, order the patient to rinse their head, and make a cauterization on the head, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the flow of affliction is from both eyes together, or in one if it is from one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skull, and be sure to make the cauterization long according to the width of the temple. And take care not to damage any sinews, and if you see too much blood coming out, stop with all your power as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision how to proceed with caution so that you do not cause harm; and never make a cauterization or operation under the two bones at the back, except for this one specific case which we are discussing.
dou cors des larmes	of the tear ducts (possibly referring to eye problems or vision issues related to tears)
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are ancient and accustomed to flowing, and are on top of the veins or near the arteries that appear on the surface of the head; and one sees that it is cold, phlegmatic superfluities, then make the cauterization I mentioned at the beginning of the affliction descending to the eyes: one cauterization inside the head, and two cauterizations on the two temples, and two cauterizations or operations under the two bones; and if there is need for more, cauterize carefully above the eyebrow with a single small cauterization.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the tear ducts from within the eyes (possibly referring to eye problems or vision issues related to tears coming from inside the eyes)
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you medicate according to what we have said in the division, and it does not bring benefit, then give the patient three bitter pills to drink; after rinsing the head, make a cauterization with olive oil in the middle of the cauterization; and make two cauterizations with the cautery called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, one near the nostrils; and be careful not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the parchment of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then the cautery of this cautery which is called "olivar" comes into play. of which there are these forms:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see fit, make two cauteries on the two eyelids as long as the eyelashes are; and do not leave your hand there except until one-third of the parchment is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	the eyelash which points the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	At times it happens that the eyelashes are converted to stinging, and they prick the eye, and one makes a cautery in two manners: namely with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or the cautery of fire commands the patient to leave the lashes alone until they are long and even; and if they prick at their birth, then he binds them so that they do not move until they are born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then the patient puts honey on them; afterward he writes a figure on the parchment of the eyes that is as the leaf of myrtle, and it is the beginning of the sign near the lashes; then he puts moistened cotton in egg-glue and muskalliance of persimmon on the eye; then he heats the cautery of which this is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterward cauterize on the figure that you have signed with a small dot and dot many times, so that the cautery is burned in that place; and the sign of the health of the eye is that you see the parchment retracted, and the lashes raised to the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the scabbing is removed; afterward heal with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the eyelashes come and the parchment is softened, then start again with the cautery on that same spot, just as you did first; and if the lashes are too long, then cauterize until the parchment rises to its natural level, and is even, and no longer pricks the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning cautery of medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; then make a parchment shape like the leaf of myrtle; then take French soap and living wax, each one-third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so it doesn't cool down, then spread it over the shape that you have made as the leaf of myrtle, and place it on paper under the eyes; and if the disease is in only one eye, then work in one, and also in both; and place moist cotton under the eye like an egg white; and the patient's face be in your hand and place your thumb showing above the medicine, and press one spot and the whole egg all the times that the patient feels the burning of the medicine, for he feels burning as well as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from your thumb.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the burning has passed, then lift up the cloth of cotton wool, and reward yourself if you see the paper lifted as well as if it were lifted by constraint of fire or incision; and if so, then it is good. If not, then put more medicine on the spot where the medicine did not work, until your works are equal, and your eyes are in order; then place moist cotton on the burn until the burns have cooled, afterwards cure the spot with ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	Et se t'est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant guerde qu'il ne chiche point de la medicine as eulx. Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l'oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu'il soit sanez; et c'est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and smallness, and according to these they have different constraints; and it is not to be blamed the right path for him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of a fistula by cauterization
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you make it cauterize in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put his head in your hand; and have the servant hold the cauterizer in such a way that it does not move, nor leave his head; then put moist cotton on one eye with egg white or persillum juice; then heat the cauterizer which is so shaped: and shape it like the tip of a quill pen; whether you wish to cauterize from one end to the other, or as an awning; but however this which is shaped will suffice for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press the fistula if it is open, and remove the purulence, and dry it; and if it is closed, work it, and remove the bowels; then place the hot cauterizer on top, and hold your hand with the cauterizer at the part near the eye, so that your hands do not make a mess; and insert the cauterizer into the fatty part of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you start with the cauterization just up to the bone, it would be good. If not, you should restart the cauterization once again, and if necessary, let it alone for 3 days; then put on moist cotton in butter, and apply the desiccative ointment until it is healed, and if after 40 days it does not heal, put on corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered; and the rest as you would have come into your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	I have a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said. Understand this about the fistula: and cut in its place; then put into the incision 1 subtle thread from a silkworm which is shaped like this:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and it is done with the quantity of a .З. of poultice; and hold your hand or camisole firmly, and do not let the patient move until the poultice has set at its oil; and it is necessary to put a moistened cotton cloth over the eye of the patient: the poultice so made is in the place of a fistula, and the blood flows by marvelous sanitation.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have said, it is good. If not, it is necessary to administer purgatives to the patient, and bring the fistula back into its proper place in the body of the patient according to what is fitting for its own location.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	It happens very often that cracks in the lips are called "fur", and likewise in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks with what we have said in divisions, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cauterizing iron according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it hastily into those cracks until it becomes as hot as it can be; afterwards, treat the place with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	an abscess of the jaw
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the jaw or to the gum or palate or to the roots of the teeth and festers and swells up and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it does not help: then it is necessary that you have a cauterizing iron according to the size of the fistula. Then boil or purge the fistula, and hold your hand until the iron is red hot and at the end of the fistula; and do this once or twice. Afterwards, cure it with what we have said in cures, until it is healed. And if it is cured thus, that's good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	from toothache or tooth sensitivity
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth ache, and you treat it with medicines but it doesn't help, then put the patient's head on your healthy one; afterwards, heat a cauterizing iron whose shape will come out like this: place a cane over the tooth. Then put hot cauterizing iron hastily inside, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth. Afterwards, lift your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your will. Afterwards, fill the patient's mouth with salty water, and have them spit it out and rinse several times.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was aching is confirmed to be healed, and the gums that were softened are restored, and the moisture that was corrupting is dried out.
de la dolor des dens	of toothache or dental pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold or there is coldness or heat in the teeth, and medicines do not help, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two ways: cauterizing with butter and cauterizing with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterizing with butter is done like this: you take a piece of cow's butter and shape it into a spoon made of iron or tin. Then take some cotton and wrap it around the point of a tent, and moisten it in melted butter, and apply it hastily to the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools down. And do this often enough that the virtues of the butter come to the root of the tooth. And if you see that the wool and cotton are wet with cold butter, then apply them to the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on top until the fire reaches the gum of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	Cauterizing with fire is done like this: you take a wooden or metal stick, thick enough that the flame won't reach the patient's mouth. Then heat the cauterizer, and when it reaches the desired shape, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer cools down. Do this often, because the pain will be gone that same day or the next.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cauterization of whatever part of the head that you wish, and according to your power; and this is the shape of the caustic:
des scrophules	scrofulous
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When scrofulous swellings are of a watery and cold moisture, and do not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the cauterizing iron with a coal fire until it reaches the desired shape, and have two openings for the smoke to escape from the other side; and place the hot cauterizing iron on the abscess once, or twice as needed, until it comes to the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cauterizing iron according to the size of the abscess, and leave it in for three days; and apply moistened cotton wool with balm so that the scab may be removed; after that, cure the area with ointments and liniments until it is healed.
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc. Aprés li fai .i. autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the humors accumulate on the channels of the womb, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be purged first with solvent medicines; after that, do a cauterization at the root of the throat, and make sure to come no closer than the throat, and do not burn deeply but only slightly. After that, do another cautery at the joint of the neck to the tip of the spine, and this is the cautery called "clavicle" from which we have the shape before; and cure the area as we said before until it is healed.
de la toust	I think I see a pattern here!
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and every illness of the womb are from cold moistures, and the patient does not have fever or heat, and it is an old sickness, then make two cauterizations on the navel in both groins; and one other cautery between the two shoulders; and let the cauteries which are called "clavile" be according to the form which was said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a .xxx., ou enqui entor. Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a .iij. rains selonc ceste forme:	And if you see, make a cauterization by piercing to the entire cauterization which is called "points" for which the form is as said before in the illness of the ears; and let the points be just up to thirty, or more or less around. Afterward cure the place according to what was said before, and let the cauteries be at three veins according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because of that the cauteries are lighter, because you make three in one stroke.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the joint of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is put back in place, but it cannot stay and returns again with a small movement that happens, as we have proven, then you must correct the first dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After that, pour oil over the patient on his back and on his chest; then lift the spoon which is inside the poultice to the arm of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, then heat up the cauterization with two nails of double iron. This is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the spoon as far as it pierces to the chest, and the fumes of the cauterization come together with four cauterizations; and because of that the cauterization is made with the cauterization which has three nails, for which the figure of the cauterization are six cauterizations; and the nerves according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cauterization which has three nails:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And once it is applied to that one nerve for which there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After that, place on the cauterization a poultice to beat with gauze; afterward make the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until he is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant. Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	And if it is dislocated on top, this thing happens often, then make a cauterization on the thick part of the cauterized spot, or many cauterizations that are piercing. For the joint is closed and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
dou cautere de pleuresin	from the treatment of pleurisy (an inflammation of the lining surrounding the lungs)
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauterizations from the roots of Aristolochia (a plant also known as birthwort) in the case of pleurisy. And do it in this manner: take a long root of Aristolochia, the longest and largest that you can find, dry it out, and make it just as thick and long as your arm; and dip it in oil, and then hold it over the fire, and cauterize one cauterization between the ribcage and the collarbone, and two small cauterizations a little lower down in the part that is below the beard; and two cauterizations between the fifth rib and the lowest one, going downwards a little. And one cauterization in the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at each side of the chest under the cauterization that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand tightly, but rather hold it open wide like when smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a .i. raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie. Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	And an ancient said that any man uses a fire cautery resembling a razor, and they heat it and put it between the ribs, until it comes to the abscess; and the pain departs, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work there is fear for the patient or he dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse according to what we have said in the division of cures, and it does not benefit, then they apply three manners of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices .iij. cauteres, ou .iiij., en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos;	Of which one manner is that you make three cauterizations, or four, in a row according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the liver cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cautery, and let the patient be lying on his back;
et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	And another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two handles, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the lever which is near the mouse, or the ribs of the patient come towards his left side, and let the elevation from which you lift the lever be according to the length of the body, and the cautery be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les .ij. ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra .iiij. Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a .iij. ners. Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	Then put the two handles on fire until the lever is perceived from the other side, and then pull out the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you see, cut off all of the cautery at three handles. After that cure when it has caused pain for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures mentioned above.
de ydropisie	dropsy (a condition characterized by swelling, typically in the legs or feet)
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes». Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres entor la boude, et .i. sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et .i. sus la mice, et .ij. derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et .i. endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	Cautery is not effective against dropsy, except for the manner that is called "asclytes". When you cure it according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not benefit, then it is necessary to make four cauteries around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the mouse, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the breast; and let the cauteries be very close to the handle of the lever.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After that, let the cautery stay open for a long time to cause pain, and do not stop the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and then healing will hasten, and both intentions (i.e. the physical and spiritual) will be together with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the trephine (a type of drill or scraper) that we have shown before. And those for the back are olive-shaped, according to what was placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	inflamation of the privy parts (i.e. a condition characterized by swelling in the genital area)
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.
