de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the deafening of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to men through deafening of a wound or a boil inside the ear, and this deafness sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is one little hole left after the perforation, and the voice sounds muffled.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	So then the one that goes deep, if it can't be seen, is due to severe inflammation in several dispositions, and the one that can be seen comes from putting the sick person's ear into the sun; and look inside: if you see a whitish congealment, then this operation has all its proper shape.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be cut and scraped before and behind all smooth, if it does not hurt the ear; if the congealment is from pus or core of the ear, then take fine tweezers and gently pick it out, until that pus is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if the congealment is deep in the ear, then take one sharp scraper and heat it a little over the fire, then put it on the core of the ear. If you feel the congealment with which the patient feels pain when hearing, pick gently, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and moisten it in Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it in rosewater, and powder on vitriol powder; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary to remove the tent and put another tent soaked in cerote made of rose oil and wax, so that the swelling may be removed; and then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding continues to come out, then dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and make use of other remedies that remove the bleeding from the wounds, such as treating with decoctions and distillations.
de la char des papieres	It seems like you've added a few lines from an old medical text.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	The following althelul that come from papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, you should stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut off a spatula from its roots; then put on the place vitriol powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not peel off, then cauterize with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after incision is worth moving; and many times repair, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are charred and do not return.
de la gresle	hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times come into the papers of the eyes things that seem like hail in shape and hardness, and for this reason is called this disease "grandine", and it is an assembly of wet masses on both sides of the paper; the work is as follows: take care if the grandine moves from one side to another, and it's a light thing to know; then make a cut on the long side, then scrape off each part lightly, then take with pincers, and cut. If you can't cut without piercing the paper slightly, it doesn't harm the patient; and if the crack is large, assemble with a seam, and cure until it heals; and if it's small, don't do anything because ointments restore it at once and in good condition.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granule is descending inside the ear towards the top part, turn the paper over and take the granule with pincers, cut it and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it doesn't harm anything; and when the granule has been cut, wash out the eye with salt water, and cure the place where it left a mark until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	meibomian gland cyst or chalazion (a type of eyelid lump)
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fatty substance that accumulates in the form of threads on the upper part of the eyelid, and it happens more often to children than to anyone else, and it causes them great discomfort in their eyes. They come with catarrh in the mornings, and they can't look at the sunlight because the tears rush into their eyes; and for that reason they lie down on their faces immediately and sleep there, and their lower eyelids are moist under their eyebrows due to the exinach which appears in the eye. And when you press the area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way to do it is that the patient places their head in your lap. Then take one linen cloth and prepare a tent-like structure in the shape of a circle, according to the amount of exinach present on each side. Place the cloth over the eye and press with your fingers from one side to the other, so that the exinach is assembled inside the circle.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take then a whole piece of linen cloth and stretch it between your two fingers from the front; and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to press on the cut, that you do not bruise all the surrounding tissue up to the eye, that you do not blind it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the skin does not open at the beginning of the cut, then stretch the cut slightly so that it opens; then pull it out as we have said, then wet linen cloths in ale and water, and place them on the wound, and then strain to bind.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there are such men who cauterize with hot oil and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains; then let him cure until he is healed. And if an abscess comes to the wound, warm poultices soothingly until he is healed.
des poilz des papieres	of papers of wool
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs that are grafted on to them and are inflamed, they harm themselves and cause various kinds of diseases such as habitual tears and moistening of the papers and albugine, so long as it is a cause of destruction of themselves; and the cure is according to four manners: or by cauterization with fire together, or by medicinal water according to what is before in the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by catheters, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your hands, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand; if it has turned, it's good; if not, put a needle with one thread above it and insert it into all of the grafted hairs on the edge of the paper where the hairs have grown. Then pull out the thread and place a small patch of cotton and linen under the paper in the area of the grafted hairs, covering the entire space from the large tear to the small one. Then take out the thread and sew above the paper a figure of lint, like the leaf of myrtle, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you see the paper swelling up.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if there is a tear that needs to be sewn up, take a large quantity of the paper according to how moist it is; then stitch along both lines you've marked and start from the large tear to the small one. And let one of the slits be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root; then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the wound, then scrape off all the excess thread. Then sew together the two lips with a stitch made with a needle and one thread of fine wool, and squeeze out the blood, and make the superfluity of the threads dry on the two stitches by any sticky things you see do this; and if not, don't bother, then leave the stitches and the strings until three or four days, then cure the wound without stitches with things that are drying and constricting. Because the paper relives itself to the solidification of the wound and its assembly, but the stitch is moist (as said by the ancients), and this is work without fear.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if there's another way: and it is that you sew the paper with a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, as we have said before, with three loose threads according to the shape which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take note of what rises to equal strength simultaneously according to the shape which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you are unable to hold the forceps, and the thing is not equal, take a needle where there is one thread, and insert it through the shape; and put another thread near the large wound, and the second thread next to the small one, and tie the two threads together evenly with your hands; then lift your hand evenly, and raise all the skin above what you have sewn, as we have counted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by stitching, and cure until it is healed; and if apostume comes to your incision, soothe it with cerote and similar soothing ointment.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	and whenever it happens that the hair of the paper is converted: it is necessary that you use what we have said of the incision; but the stitch in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds in the tail is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two thin strings also long as the length of the paper and the width of the space between them; and take hold of the two ends of the threads on each side; then assemble one and the other carefully above what rises from the oil paper, and strain out the two stitches from both parts together; and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and become black and wither, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it delays, take a small amount of force and cure until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is removed, and the hair will no longer be present; and this is the shape of the two stitches that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is as follows: take a thin needle, and insert one thread of fine silk into it; then take the two ends and tie them together carefully, making sure the length of the threads is about a palm's width. Then, place another thin thread of silk alongside the first one, and tie the end of the thread. Put the patient's head on the thread, and let it be in the sun so that the procedure is clarified, as this is a delicate and small procedure. Insert the needle into the root of the hair closest to the paper, and make a hole quickly until you can draw it out above the natural hair. Then, pull out the natural hair with the thread attached to it, if there is one or two or three or more hairs; then pull your hand gently until all the hairs come out together with the thread in the paper.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the thread is pulled out and the hairs do not come with it, you will pull the thread underneath all the thread that you have placed, until the thread comes out from above through the small hole and you can see it with your eyes. Then, once you have pulled out the thread and the hair, close the eye and let it be closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and a new skin grows over it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the inflammation of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or inflammation comes to the eye, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. It happens suddenly due to a wound, cut, or burn, and by similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the way to treat it is that you split open the wound and separate its edges, and put in linen tents, and tie them until it heals; and it's not necessary for you to use things that dry out and constrict during its treatment. Because if you do this, the disease will come back worse than the first time; but it works with soothing things, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or almond oil cooked, and ointments made from daquilon melted in any oil, and you envelop a tent with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you keep watch so that it does not heal in the same form as before; and these operations which we have said are nothing other than precautions against this disease, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh (or ulcer) that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is underneath the eye and is truly called "axacrati", which is a natural and accidental condition. The accident comes from a wound, cut, or burn, and similar things; and the way to treat it is that you take a needle with two threads, insert the needle into the flesh, and make it pierce through the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread goes into both holes of the flesh. Then place the flesh over the entire length of the needle, and sew it with a seam as wide as a thumb.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the paper comes back in that shape, it's good. If not, take a razor and place it in the incision, and turn the paper over, and make two slits or cuts on either side within the paper; and have the holes of the two slits be at the two angles of the incision that you sewed. And make the edges so that when they are assembled, the figure will be like a letter that has the name "Jgriesche". Then remove that flesh, according to the size of its sides below, from what is under the paper; then join together the two severed parts and sew them with a thread of linen. And then cure it with the medicines we have said, and with tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from an incision or cut or burn, it is fitting that you make a straight incision underneath the layers of paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said. And the operation should be done in accordance with the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form. The wise masters prepare an instrument from all their power so that they can make the figure return to its natural shape. And the patients themselves, according to what is fitting for treatment and instruments, and in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the suddenness of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this wound has in many men in the same manner that the paper above is stuck with the white of egg, and cannot move or do its natural activities, then it is necessary for you to put the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and let it be so fine, not too sharp nor too cutaneous, that the patient cannot suffer if the saw blade cuts into the eye; and your incision, from which you scrape off this assembly, should be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and the entire assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye a salted water is applied, and a sweet wine is lifted up, and a cordial; then put between the paper and the eye a linen cloth, and place on the eye wool soaked in egg white; and after the third day use of the cordial and other similar things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	the corner of the eyelid
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It is known that the corner of the eyelid is in two ways: it is nerve-like and resembles a hard yellowish scab, and another which is not nerve-like, but rather resembles frozen white moisture, so that when one touches it with iron and tries to pierce it with needles, it cannot be pierced; and both appearances begin towards the large tear sac, and grow little by little until it covers all the eye and its light and movement.

de la fistule de l’oil	It seems that the text has come to an end with "de la fistule de l'oil", which means "of the eye abscess" or "fistula of the eye". This is likely a medical term from the Middle Ages, referring to a condition where there is an abnormal connection or channel between the inside and outside of the eye.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Li mire (a surgeon) call it "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and with hot medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is an artifice in it that you must cut on top of the abscess, where it should die, and drain out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.

de la bowe de l’oil	Of the lower part of the eye (i.e. the conjunctiva or the sclera).
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This illness called "alcunnati" is nothing other than the conjunctiva or the membrane that gathers in the eye, resembling a thread descending, and it's not a thread; the manner of its appearance is as follows: you have the patient sit on a well-made and straight chair, then take his head between your hands from both sides, and lift up his eyelid until you see the conjunctiva or membrane come up to your eyes; then pierce it with a fine needle, and don't let it descend again and be dislodged by the light, and have the patient see things as he normally would; and if it doesn't descend below, know that it's a thread (i.e. not actually conjunctiva), and if the descent of the membrane is not as we said, then have the patient sit in your hands, then take the fine needle and pierce through the corneal membrane one spot at a time, by continuing from the conjunctiva to the cornea and the cornea itself, until the membrane issues; and when it has issued, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then cure him with another treatment until he is healed.

de la char sor le neis	of the flesh above the navel
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	There are various kinds of flesh lumps that grow on the body, some of which resemble scorpions in shape; and some have a colored lump with bright color, and others have a soft bone-like lump. In one of these kinds of lumps that is soft, not hardened, you should make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; open their nostrils, and let out the contents of the lump through them, then hold what you can catch with the pointed part of a knife on either side until you know the lump is entirely loosened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that you cannot cut out, open it all up with thin, sharp instruments; until nothing is left. If the abscess bursts on its own, or opens without your doing anything to it, then let it heal itself, and the scabs will come off as they should. And if it's malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize them until the pain is extinguished, and all the flesh lumps are cut out; then pour vinegar or wine into it.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the abscess doesn't open and its liquid flows up to the palate, you'll know it's healed. And if the liquid doesn't drain as it should, then you'll know that there is an accumulation of flesh in the bone above; for the instruments can't cut through: at that point, you must put a thread of linen, about the size of your finger, and not too thick, with between each knot a space of one or two fingers. Put the patient's nose over the end of the thread near their face, and breathe in strongly until the liquid comes out through the nose into the mouth; this is often done by children at school, and it's an easy thing to do for someone who wants to do it. Then take the part that comes out the nose with one hand, and the other part that comes out the mouth with the other hand, and pull them out slowly while keeping the thread taut between your hands. Do this until you know that the knots have corrupted all the flesh, then pull out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back into the abscess as before. Do this for three days or more, until the poultice corrodes everything remaining of flesh; and then put a clean linen cloth over the abscess for several days until it is healed, and if necessary use dry medicines; and this is the form of the instrument to drain the head, with which one distills oils and medicines into the abscess.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it can be made of silver or lead, resembling an open lantern like a candle, and it is used in the same way. And if you see fit, make a closed lantern, and have the instrument full to purge the head; and let there be a handle at the top to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the skin above the navel
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Sometimes a disease called "telul" arises on the navel and grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible with the naked eye; and therefore you should have it removed from the beginning, and cut out all of the flesh around it, then apply the hot cautery or medicine on top of it; and if one delays cutting it until it has grown large, beware that it may be hard, of foul color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron at all because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut into it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of clean appearance, not of foul color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then the patient will feel empty and the wound will heal well with things drying up and constricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the navel is cut open and cleaned
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is said that when a solution of concoction comes to one of these cartilaginous membranes, it is of little use, in some men. Therefore, when this happens to anyone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then close the two lips together at a seam, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated from each other on one side or both, it is necessary that you scrape off all the parts of their edge until they heal, then assemble the two lips together at a seam, and bind them, and sprinkle on top powdered dragon's blood and frankincense; and put on top of the powders a piece of plugging plaster, strong or another soldering plaster, and leave it until it hardens by itself, then cure with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the skin with:
des apostemes des levres	Abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home they often get abscesses in the lips that are hard and resemble grains of mustard, smaller and larger ones; then you should turn your lips inside out, and cut each one with a needle and cauterize it with vinegar so that the wound is closed; and then let the lip heal on its own, and treat the area with dry things until it's healed.
de la char des gencives	from the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often there is gum tissue that grows on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; if it needs to be removed, you should hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and let blood or pus come out; then apply vinegar to the area, or other constricting and drying powders; and if that gum tissue comes back after being incised, and often does, you should cut it a second time and cauterize it: if it doesn't come back after being cauterized, those are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellowish and green, until corruption comes to the gum, and it is stinking. You should make the patient sit in your hands, and their eyes be on you, and pull out the teeth or scabs as soon as they appear, until there is nothing left; and do the same with the blackness and yellowness and greenish color and other spots, until they are clean. And if you take out what is at the first reason, it's good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have cleaned everything. And know that teeth need various forms of instruments to be cleaned, according to how the work shows it, because the scrapers used to scrape away from the teeth have other shapes than those used to scrape between them; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as possible to extract it, because it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high risk that there is no excuse for extracting. (This text suggests that the medieval dentist was being cautious and advising patients to delay extraction, possibly in an effort to avoid taking out teeth unnecessarily.)
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then, when the patient is compelled to have it extracted, you should be certain of which tooth is to be taken out. Many times pain has deceived the patient, and they think that the good tooth is the one causing them pain, and so they extract the good tooth; but, nevertheless, the bad tooth remains, for we have already warned them about such saints. And when you are well aware of which tooth is to be extracted, you should scrape around the tooth on all sides with a spatula made strong to protect the gum from all parts; then move it with your thumbs or delicate tweezers at the first notch and notch, until they are well separated; then tighten the tweezers. And have the patient's eye in your sight between your knees, and hold their hand steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the correct tooth with no breaking, and if it does not fall out, take one of these instruments and push it gently into both sides, and move it as you did first. And if the tooth is pierced and eaten, then it is necessary that you fill it with cloths, there where the perforation is; and if you must strain it subtly with tweezers, so that it does not break when straining; and it is very important to work carefully around the gum for loosing the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take good care that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and the patient will feel more severe pain from the root than the first; And take care that you do not act like the ignorant sages who by their haste and boldness sometimes break the tooth, and do not bring about what we have told you; but often cause great suffering with the roots remaining or the tooth broken, as we have so often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with vinegar or oil of sage and saffron; and if bleeding decorum comes out, which often happens, fill the place with vitriol powder; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	It seems like the text is describing a specific type of dental instrument used to extract teeth. The translation continues:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick limbs so that they do not bend at all, and let them be iron plates well made, and let them be held by teeth to keep them in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root of the tooth is exposed on the outside, you should put moistened cotton or grease on the place, i.e., for a day or two, until the place becomes soft, then insert the pliers called "algefri", by which the tooth seems to be bitten like a dog; and they are made inside in the same shape as a file and that's its form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with those pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", i.e., pincers, by which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, you should use all the instruments, by which these shapes come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if that doesn't help with this instrument that has two rings, by which this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other bandages that are placed in front of the teeth, and this instrument which resembles large pincers, the shape of which is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is useful only in that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for the teeth; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise, skilled masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their work and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach a single instrument because of the diversity of them; and one should not break the chariot or the other bones unless it is necessary, or if he seeks the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and with gestures, the form of which is as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they are large and well-holding to hold the bone so it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place of the medicines fitting for this, and if there is putridness in the bone and it is small, then let all of this instrument be used:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural shape and the form is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know whether the tooth is newly grown after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be filed or smoothed: then make a groove. And if it is uneven with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is as follows, and resembles one small beak, and is made of iron with an acute point at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in one's hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to be filed, take a file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like sharpening needles; and when you sharpen the point of a tooth, do it little by little in light hands so that it does not move until it takes shape; then finish with a smooth plane, and if the teeth are too sharp and hurt the tongue, you must whet the roughness until they are even, so that they do not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the front tooth is loose due to a blow or fall, and the patient cannot press on it without wincing, and you have tried treating it with restraining medicines, but they are not effective; then you must restrain it with a thread of gold, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold ones never change; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are misaligned, take the thread and insert it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth in between them, as many as there are, until they reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then start wrapping the covering again from where you started, and gently and carefully tighten your hand until it does not move anymore; and let your knot be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then clip off the loose ends of the thread with tweezers and assemble them, and insert them between the healthy teeth, and place them so that they do not hurt the tongue; and then leave them tightly in place as long as possible, and if they come loose or the threads break, you should tighten it with another thread; if it stays in place and serves its purpose for a long time, this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth and the two loose ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, you should replace it in its place, fresh from the bone, just as we have said; and let no one who is not skilled and careful intervene; and sometimes the shape of a jawbone's tooth is formed, and it is placed in the location where the defect is, and it is tightened just as we have said, and it stays in place and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to uncover the ligature of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Whenever it is the ligature that comes from under the tongue by nature or from a healed wound; or by accident of stitched flesh; and the work is such as to open the mouth of the patient, and have his head in thy hand, and lift up the tongue; then uncover the nervous ligament on the side, so much as to dislocate the tongue from its dwelling place, and if there is hardness or knot, and it's from a sudden wound, then put an unguent and cover the large ligament; and take care that the fissure not be too deep down, for the artery which is below; and when thou hast done this, then lift up the powder of rose and eggshell, or cold water, and put under the tongue a tent of linen; and let the patient bleed each night, so the wound may not close. And if there comes bleeding from the vein, then put vitriol plaster on top of the wound; and if the blood stops, then cauterize it with lentiginous cautery, which is good for such things; then cure him with another remedy until he be whole.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the growth is white or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards the groin, and there is moisture, then throw away the unguent, and make a fine paste with vinegar, and deliver him from both sides; and if the bleeding stops at thy work, then put vitriol plaster on top until it be stanchied, then return to thy work until thou hast removed all impurity; then lift up the powder of eggshell and rosewater, and cure him with other remedies until he be whole.
des apostemes de la gorge	Il semble que le texte soit une traduction ou un résumé d'une partie du "Régime du corps" attribué à Guy de Chauliac, médecin de Charles V du roi d'Arles (1347-1380).
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes there comes within the throat swellings called "godath", and they are properly called .ij. almonds; and when you treat them, as we said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small size and green color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for the bleeding; but leave it alone until it is dead, and then you will take it out, or it would break off by itself; and if it is of white color like a pear, and the root is subtle, have ready the instrument to cut it, but look first if the abscess has calmed down and is appeased. Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and your hands be clean, and prepare the mouth and take hold of the silver between his hands, and press the tongue below the whole instrument, which is its shape; and be made of silver or fine lead just like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue against the whole instrument, and you see the abscess, then take a wick and stick it in the almond, and the thread will be above as much as you can; and leave nothing of the threads with it, then cut at the instrument, which is its shape, that looks like a fist; and although the tip is curved, and one end the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or lead:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	Je pense que j'ai compris la traduction ! Voici :
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it should be cut on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after incision gargle the patient with hot water and warm oil, and scented waters which cause blood to flow out, so gargle the patient with water or with cooked pomace of pomegranates, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then cure as long as it is needed; and sometimes other swellings appear in the throat than the two almonds, so cut them in the same way as the two almonds are joined.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had appeared in the throat, namely one of small size; and it had grown well inside to close up almost all the throat, so that the woman could not exhale because of the conduit being blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have been dead if she had remained like that for a day or two. And the abscess was I so swollen that two rains had been made through the two outlets of it. I hastened then, and inserted in one an onion, then the thread came out, and took out a great portion of pus; then I refixed the other part to the other outlet of the abscess, and closed the woman's mouth and pressed her tongue; after that I inserted the onion into the abscess and cut a part of it, and there came out only a small amount of blood; and thus was unblocked the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink hot water and then wine, and did not stop cutting out from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess reappeared every day, and filled up the place I had emptied, until it grew quite large; at that point I stitched it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing further; and I left those places, and only God knew what to do with her after me.
de l’uve	It seems like you're trying to translate something from an old language or text.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. For there is great peril on the patient.
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Take the instrument that is used for putting on medication, such as a spoon or a syringe, and put the instrument to all of the medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie down on their side so that the saliva and mucus from their mouth go into the medicine inside, so it does not descend to the throat and the wound; then hold your hand over all of the medicine and press it onto the eye for the amount of time of half an hour, until you see it darken and the irritations from the medicine are calmed down. And if you see anything, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument into all of the cotton on the back of it, so that the cotton hardens onto the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and wait for later.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner: take camomile and yarrow and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put ash in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with strong earth, and inside the pot have a tool fashioned like a comb according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. And it should be of silver or lead, and one of the keys is placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapour rises to the eye through the pipe, until the eye is mortified; afterwards it recedes several times, until the eye dries, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the hot aposteme's coming out, for many things happen; and don't do it either before the hot aposteme has cooled down. If they insert it downwards, or pull it out at all the instrument in equal parts, until it is completely out.
de la sansue de la gorge	Il semble que nous ayons terminé l'extrait. Voici une traduction plus complète et claire du texte :
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes medicine is used for bloodletting, as I have said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when it does not benefit, then look into the patient's throat by sunlight, and press their tongue with the instrument that I told you to use. And if you see the blood, take it all, i.e., a small amount of an inch or two, or fine tweezers that are worth it. And if this is not useful, then take a long string, and put it in the patient's throat, then insert one hot iron at the end of the string, and do this often. And if the patient has fever all day, then take a full glass of cold water, and open their mouth, and pour it into their mouth without swallowing, and move their tongue around with their hand; and as soon as the blood sees the water, it will fall.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. And if it does not fall as we have said, then let the patient sniff with assafetida at the instrument that I told you in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, because it will come out soon. And the manner of fumigation is that you take a pot where there are hot coals, and it should be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and in one of the holes of the cloth should be the instrument; then throw your fumigation into it, and the patient puts the end of the string in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not come out, but comes up to the blood; and now the blood will fall, and if it does not fall, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient feel thirsty, and eat salty things and suchlike, and do not drink water; and then it is necessary for the illness to go away by this treatment.
