mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon;	but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the knee, you tie to the thigh of the woman, then fumigate with trephine ointment. (This suggests a more drastic treatment, possibly involving surgery or a specialized medical procedure)
si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	but it will give relief and put her right again, and make her better. Nevertheless, when she has purged herself, a foul smell comes from the stomach and head, and harms the woman. (This suggests that while the treatment may be effective in some cases, it can also have negative consequences or side effects)
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So then it is necessary to do good fumigations for her: none of the ancients have ever tried fumigation with cabbage and dried figs. (This suggests that a specific type of fumigation, using cabbage and dried figs, may be beneficial in this case)
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman at retention of flowers and of the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu;	And it is to behold a swelling similar to a chain, and one places the head of it subtly in its natural place, and the joints are large over the fire;
et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	and let the fumigation be above the coals, and the scab so long as it is eaten away, and another one begins again.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not had their foundation pierced, but rather it has been stifled by subtle flux.
si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche;	So it is convenient to the belly that she pierces that flux at its due time, and does not pierce itself with sharp spatula, and guard the ligament so that it does not touch it.
puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put on linen soaked in wine and oil, then cure with salve until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it has closed again, then put or make a poultice with a cord of linen, and let it stay for days, and have it removed when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And whenever this stoppage comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; it is convenient to close that suddenness: if it is cured, as we have said of the cord of linen.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in the fundament (i.e. the anus)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Fistulas that come from under the fundament (i.e. the anus) are nodular and grow more, than those that come from outside the fundament or in the space between the two parts.
si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe,	if it has a fistula or several; and when that nodulation is old, it works out, and leaves more moisture or a white or subtle pus.
et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	and sometimes these fistulas are purulent; and they are known by those that come out or are ejected or ventilated when the sick person makes an evacuation, and perhaps with a sudden jump of a worm.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if it has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis; and reach just to the junction of the thigh, and just to the back of the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant:	And thus one knows the purulent fistula at the fundament, and not purulent.
et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	and it is that you press your thumb or fundament, and insert a fine needle of lead or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou .i. poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit;	And if it has tortuosity, then tie on a tight thread of thin linen, or one horsehair, as long as you feel the thread or hair at your fingertip;
et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit:	and if you don't feel it, and there is no purulent discharge nor windy or worm-like condition, as we have said:
saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	know that it does not perforate; hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has perforated just to the bladder or just to the urethra's channel, then it lets out urine, and cannot be stitched together by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu;	If it has perforated just to the crotch's jointure, then the thread comes out just at the place.
s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement;	if there is no tortuosity and the discovery of pain around it, then it is that it will go down to the groin, and it does not help by medicine nor stitching with anointing.
et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	and in these perforated fistulas there is no strong cure other than labor, and the vainness of foolish practitioners who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit,	In that which is not perforated nor old, there is hope for health by iron, as I have proved.
et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre;	and it is that the sick person lies between your hands on their back; and lifts up their legs as high as their crotch, and has their crotch inclined towards their belly.
puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then put in an iron thread, or a linen one if there is tortuosity, as long as you know the thread comes to;
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the sick person feels it around the fundament, then it is fitting that you put in your index finger.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	if they then sense that the thread has perforated it, and you discover that there is something between your finger's tip and the skin or flesh, then know that it is perforated.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	if not so, then there's no hope of healing it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	It is always said that some can be healed well, but this is rare.
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and the help we do there, it is that we cauterize with a fine iron rod according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before.
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and put it all hot in the fistula, as far as it will go up to the fundament; and do this two or three times, until you know that those charred tissues are burnt, which are similar to a bird's feather.
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	and then the cure with wet threads in honey, as long as those burnt things ooze out; and then the cure with anointing ointment, healing the wound and uniting it.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If it is thus healed, that's good. If not, otherwise it cannot be healed. (Note: this text seems to be a medieval medical recipe or treatment for a fistula, and the language is somewhat archaic)
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the thread goes in and doesn't pierce as far as the fundament, and between your finger and the thread is a thick covering of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula to that which is outside the covering of the wound;
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If the tip of the abscess bursts at the beginning, and you block it again before the tent, and apply the cautery afterwards, until it comes to the top of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	and the abscess will be released from the body, and it will heal; then remove those false carbuncles that look like a bird's feather, and none of them will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the poison spreads towards you, and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For cauterizing with fire assembles two good things: that is to say, the drying of those false humors and the coagulation of blood and the scorching of moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	then treat with tents made of wet butter or cheese broth, until the abscess gushes out below, and let the burned humors flow into the bowel.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	then treat the wound with sudden ointments that harden rough skin, and they are dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed, then it does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the bottom of the fundament and is distant from the body, then block it with a cork or plug at the fundament, and question those.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the abscess and it bursts between two things, whether it's the cloth or the syphac or humors, or it is near to bursting, if there are no ulcers except what shows faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three manners:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	You cauterize it as we have said, or you chop it right down to the bottom, or if you can just try to insert and treat it first.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and don't go too deep, that you cut the ligament that holds the foundation, and comes the hemorrhage by the involuntary sense;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then treat it, as we have said.
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	perhaps it will be sound, or you take off that covering and clean it then because it is cut near the foundation, either by tenting or with another instrument appointed.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then scrape out that dead flesh which is in the wound, as much as you can.
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and to remain the fistula in the part outward from the foundation; if it is easier thing for the sick person.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And once its fistulas according to this manner: and is when you pokes the tent in the fistula, and it is or costed on the foundation near the skin above.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	if take a tent pierced at the head according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put 1. thread twisted in 2, and I insert the tent into all the thread in the fistula as far as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is pierced in the edge of the foundation inside, then draw out the thread from that perforated one, so that you insert your finger or the foundation.
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	and draw out the head of the thread, and join together the two heads together, and bind one to the other, and leave it for one day or two;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	and then bind it at any time, until the threads have cut through those char things that are between them, and they discharge.
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	then treat the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then make it pierce in all ways that you can, as long as it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not necessary to make it pierce so deep that the thread cuts through, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the spatula-like spine that one makes the fistula with is quite rough from one end and tapering.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other side not at all, for which reason we do not cut those things that should not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the sinewy ones.
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Sinews are in two ways: or they are inside the foundation, as grains of resin, and there are small ones and large ones, and in a short time they heal over.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and there is one or more, and they are outside the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are outside have a lot of moisture.
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	and in a short time they become quite watery or quite bloody, and have the color of raw flesh.
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the treatment for those that are inside the foundation is that you command the patient to sit up in order to bring the contents out, until the foundations become empty and the threads appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and you have pincers or hold it with your fingernail, then cut them at their roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the sinews cannot hold them because of their moisture, then take them in one cloth, or cotton, or a piece of linen.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	and pull them out with your fingers, then cut them, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of cauterization.
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize them as is said in the treatise on cauterization, and then cure them with other treatments until they are healed.
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundations cannot come out, then purge the patient with a harsh and bitter purgative to cleanse what is in the foundation, so that it may come out clearly.
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	if the patient is willing and if the threads are outside of the foundation, then the treatment is light.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	and that you take them with your fingernail or pincers and cut them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and the patient should fear no incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	It is necessary that you bring the suture according to this manner: take one twisted thread and insert it into an awl, and then pull the thread up and make the awl pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread over the awl.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and it is of the right width; and strain the thread tightly, then twist the thread, and pull out the awl, and do thus with all the others, and leave one to correct any excess blood.
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	then place over the foundation one moist cloth soaked in olive oil or resin, and place it over the wound, and command the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then let them be until they cease bleeding, and when they have stopped, treat them with ointment and other treatments, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the fistula or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there has been dryness of the fistula in the intestine, and by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine is useless.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you cut away at the top with a spatula or your fingernail the scab that does not allow it to moisten.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then treat it until it is sound, as is necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot become sound, then repeat the scraping more strongly than before, until it heals much and scabs over.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	of the fistula (or a sudden onset of it)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	A furuncle is a small false appearance on the body, and it goes deep into the flesh.
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	and at times the boil bursts and the abscess comes out in the same way as a furuncle, and it appears all over the body, and more so in the arms than any other place.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is that you take a cord made from an owl's feather or a strong goose quill and place it on the furuncle, until the circle turns purple all around.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand in a full circle with the cord until you cut all around the furuncle and put it into depth, and extract the boil from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is necessary, do the same with a cord of bronze or iron in this shape, and be subtle under and thread on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	don't pierce it, so that it can be held with the fingers, and press it. And if you see that it is necessary, cauterize the furuncle, as is written in the treatise on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a purgative
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times they make a purgative of silver or mercury, or molten bronze or copper, and at times they make these small and large instruments in the same way as they are intended.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	So those that are made for the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a purgative, whether small or large, is as follows: the belly is closed in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it has a small opening or the belly is closed, as you see, and one end is pierced inside, and on one side there are two holes, and on the other, one.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the belly or pouch is filled with medicines from a animal bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	and between each hole there is a small space, then insert into these holes one strong thread of twisted wire or iron in ten or eleven turns around, and close the belly as if it were a sack.
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and when the medicines are inside, tie the instrument with a strong thread in front, then purge; and this is the form of a plug.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And the medicines should not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the top of the purgative with oil or egg yolk or something similar, then insert it gently.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	then the servants should hold the patient's legs together with both hands until it is completely empty, then pull out the purgative and lift the patient's legs up to the bed.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and if the medicines want to come out, then hold it as tight as possible; and if the patient sleeps for a night completely, it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge the patient for the disease of purging the belly, and the medicines hurry to come out, then repeat it until they are healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por .i. enfant;	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or have grown, then the purgative should be as subtle as for a child.
et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	and this is the form of a gentle purgative whose skin is strained tight.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the section on the treatment of wounds; now we will say the treatments for hands and medicine, according to fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse in accordance with how they were made, and in accordance with the place or location where the wound was made, and what they were made by.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made are by sharpness of stone, and the cut of a sword or knife, or lance or fist or seat, or similar things.
ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres;	or that are made according to the place of the body, such as a wound that bleeds on the neck, or on the head, or on the chest, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar members.
et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from sharpness of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large.
et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree;	and you doubt the wound is hot with an apostema, if it does so quickly heal itself with a cephalic remedy itself, and there comes pus from the wound, and the wound heals in contrast to the injured part.
et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	and abstain the patient from drinking wine and eating heavy meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char;	And if it does not heal, then reduce the patient's food and do not let them drink wine or eat meat.
et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice;	and put on the wound a poultice, if hot apostemes come, made with a moist cloth in olive oil or vinegar.
et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés;	and if there is no hot apostema, then put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood and has not been affected by the air, a powder that I will speak of shortly.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if the wound has become festering, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the edges cannot be closed by stitching, then close them with sutures, just as I will say about the belly wounds, in the chapter on suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir,	And if the wound is exposed to the bone and it bleeds and only holds together by a small amount of flesh, then scrape it out. Then treat the wound with medicine, and cover it with hard tissue in place of skin.
et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	and command the patient to eat heavy foods, such as roasted meat and bread, also chickens and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure;	And if you find pus in the skin that has not reached the bone, scrape out all the pus and throw away the dead tissue, then treat it.
et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil;	and if there is a vein or artery in the wound that needs to be tied off and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then ligate the artery, and if you find it, untwist it and tie it with a thread.
et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and that you put on this powder which heals even when the wound has become festering.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the manner of making this powder is: take one part of incense; dragon's blood two parts; and live calamine three parts, and grind it finely.
et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc;	and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it firmly until it dries well and joins together with all its blood.
et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	and then bind it tightly, and leave it to come off itself if it swells, for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at times one makes this mixture of calamine alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the wound has become festering and inflamed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the fire has made the wound festering, even in its depth, then do not put on this powder.
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	but instead put on some digestive ointments, or poultices made from barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it discharges pus.
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if the bone breakage comes with the wound and it is small, then extract it with thin tweezers.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	and I will tell you shortly about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no distinction between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it is the nerves, then there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not put anything restraining on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them withdraw.
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member.
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but apply a soothing medicine to it, such as calamine dissolved in sweet water and mixed with rose oil, and also cucumber juice dissolved in sweet water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and tie it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and they are swollen and full of pus, then puncture them lower down.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	and if the artery is cut and bleeding occurs, then tie it off, bind it, and cauterize it as needed.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	and if the spinal cord or the vertebra is cut, and the conduit is kept, by which the flesh goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	so sew the vertebra above the spinal cord, and do not touch the throat, but put it back in its natural position.
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then bind it tightly and leave it for some days, then treat it with ointments of the same kind until it is healed.
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then scrape it out.
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, then remove them all that you can, and those that you cannot, leave them until the wound becomes purulent.
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and then stitch it up and bind the end tightly.
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has formed an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it is a cut from a lance or knife and the wound is deep, look to see if there are signs of putridity in the patient's breath, then know that the wound is mortal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it is not deep and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put on the powder at first hour, nor bind it tightly for the bleeding that does not stop in depth.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and the patient recovers to their heart and dies.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but I put an attractive ointment on it, and bind it two times a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	and if you do not have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out the moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	if there is no convulsion, bad heart trembling, or severe pain, then it is not mortal.
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	and when you see the good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then sew it up and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it cannot heal and works, then know that there is an abscess; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is a cut from a sword or knife and it is superficial, or worse on the back, treat it as one would for wounds on the front.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	if it is large, then sew it up; if it is small, treat it with powder; and if it has become embedded in the bone and cut into fragments, then scrape out the wound and remove any fragments that are loose.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	and if they cannot be removed, then let the wound become purulent, so that it will draw out the fragments.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgments are as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of intestinal rupture.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly are great, middle-sized, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	from a large wound where sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines are cut, by which their entry is obstructed.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	and the suturing is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse for a small wound than for a large one.
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	because of this, they reinsert the intestines with more care, and do not insert them in cold pieces by piece.
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	because the intestines swell as soon as they feel the cold, so they are inserted with more care.
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	and because of this, it is better to treat the small wound, because one must rinse the intestine back to its place with more care than the other two.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	And know that the rupture of the belly is in three manners:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	the two common wounds occur in the suturing of the belly,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and the suturing of other wounds of the body and two other specific suturings are common to other wounds.
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	and anyway they are more proper with the suturing of the belly, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I will follow your instructions exactly.
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	and what needs to be done is this: it is by one of the two manners:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or through the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	or because the intestines are inflamed by cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	soak a sponge or one cloth made from linen in hot water only,
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or boil it in water of saponaria and cypress and spike.
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	and wrap the intestine so long as the swelling is removed;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	and once this has been done, it should be restrained and is moved only to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling departing, then moisten the intestine with hot water or ale and cook the onions.
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	for by that is allayed the entry to a little thing;
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	and if it cannot enter, then make a small pouch of the wound with the instrument with which we scrape off hemorrhoids;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first cure is moved that the stitch,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we must not stitch it without great necessity, for there may not be one.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to cut it:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut within in the curve and without no, and behold here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	so put it back there according to its natural shape in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you are able, for this is worth a try.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the lower part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it's good that you make the patient lie on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the lower part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	so raise his head and chest higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two sides,
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	so place your intent that the injured part be higher than the other;
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is good to remember what I say in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, apply the things that you are accustomed to.
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	then take between your hands one pus-filled minister who covers all the rupture with his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and close the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and this is the common manner of stitching.
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave at the head of the wound a good two fingers' space, and put in a needle where it has a strong thread.
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two ends of the skin with the two ends of the suture.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is under the skin inside, until you make it pierce from that side.
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and tie the two ends of the suture together four times;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then twist a doubled thread around the needle from both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and then tie the two ends of the wound together gently,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave a good two fingers' space, and put in another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread so as you have tied the first needle.
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do this with the needles, according to what you need.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is bound up.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and let the needles be small and fine, as well as thick ones,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because the fine needles penetrate all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter at all:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	so it is good that they are fine.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it does not help to thrust the needles too far out of the flesh and the skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	for they do not pierce but rather open up the wound in front of the suture.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut off the ends of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient at night.
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and I put threads or cloth strips on the ends of the needles to hold them in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them so until the wound is sewn up;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds.
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it suffices to have one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second suture, that is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you tie the two ends of the skin and the two ends of the suture together with one needle where there is a strong fine thread.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced these ends all four times,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then turn the needle back at the part where you began, in the manner that one sews clothes.
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave space between each suture the width of a small thumb.
ceste costure sevent li home,	this suture is known to men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I sewed up a wound on the belly of a man.
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who had been wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's width in length.
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and the intestines were well two palms' width in length, protruding outwards.
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back the intestines then, after it had been four and twenty hours open,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was sewn up in just fifteen days, and he healed, and was whole again.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the doctors had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and they did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I put old cotton wool on top of the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper manners of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and thrust it from outside through to the inside.
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced through the skin straight through, then tie the end of the thread or cord where you thrust in the needle.
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side, from inside to outside.
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew just as the furrier makes a pelt.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave it once in one place and then pick it up again from the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Galien calls properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is that in which one joins the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the thread to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle or a point of fine cord nearby and make it pierce just that place.
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the thread.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from outside through to the inside again.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	with the two ends of the thread still.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce from outside through to the inside, in two other threads of fine cord that are on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second manner of stitching and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien himself said these words, and everyone testifies to them.
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	that the belly should be sewn with two needles, where there is thread in each one.
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one must put one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew leather.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when a rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more difficult than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the fresh wound with all its blood still in it, just as if fire had changed it.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the flesh, and on top of that powdering charcoal.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the fire has changed it, then put on some salve that is present, until the wound closes.
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and cut the thread, and sew the thread, and the cord together again.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound just as the others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you have no medicine, then put on old cotton, immediately when it starts to close up.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and turn it over twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you have no need for other medicine in most simple cases of wounds;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound may become an abscess on the main members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	it is advisable to boil light linen in hot temperate oil or in rose oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and put it around the pustules and under the armpits.
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if it feels pain or irritation in the bowels, and many times has happened,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then use enema of black wine to cleanse them, and similarly if the irritation comes just up to the intestine.
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The small intestine, also called "jeune", cannot heal when it is wounded.
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and this is because of the fragility of its veins and because of the subtlety of all its parts and the proximity of their nature to that of the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the gut protrudes from the wound, put it back in place just like the intestine, while it is still fresh.
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become green or black, then it is advisable to bind the place that is black, so that no bleeding occurs.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	for there are veins and arteries.
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cover what is between the bandage.
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and put the two ends hanging from below the wound down to outside to relieve the extraction when the gut slips out and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	it can be restored in some people.
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I have seen that a man was wounded with a lance to the belly;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became gangrenous and turned into a fistula, and there came out pus and wind.
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I treated him as I knew how, and did not cease to subtlety until he was healed, and the place closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw it heal, I doubted that the sickness had caused harm in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no harm, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking.
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and some experienced ones said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take a piece of linen of great thickness, then join the edges of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the linen has covered the mouth of it, put it on top of the two lips.
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that its mouth is sewn shut.
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then wrap the head around it and this holds so that it cannot be untied.
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another strip of linen behind in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered.
et cout la plaie.	and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This method holds fast in the intestine and brings no harm to the sick person.
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and if one can bind the intestine with a fine thread that is wrapped around the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread that has been stripped of its fat.
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this thread a thin strip of linen twine turned,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread into the needle and sew up the intestine, and turn it back to its natural position.
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this manner of stitching with linen is not better than by the way of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, or even in one of the main intestines, then there is no cure nor healing, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes gangrenous, is universally called "fistula".
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and likewise when it is closed and heals over.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the natural hardness of bone or flesh, where there is no pain felt,
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also closed like the feathers of a bird.
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it bursts open and heals over, and other times it becomes more swollen.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes small and other times large.
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of the classification of wounds that every wound which is not healed and has no flesh,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is nothing other than by one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	that is to say, by the smallness of the blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness.
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hardened flesh inside and on the edges that does not allow fresh flesh to grow.
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or there is too much swelling.
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the place is corrupt and the matter has bad quality.
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in its treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because of the corruption it is a manner of plague.
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because of its property in the region, the digestion is slow and the healing is late, and it tends to decay by nature.
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or there are veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And now it is fitting that I make you aware of the treatment of fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all parts of the body.
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from the main veins, and arteries, and nerves.
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or in the thread, or intestine, or bladder, or in any of the ribs.
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or on the spine of the back, or in any of the joints of the hands or feet.
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and it is so that it comes to the property of the main member, and to similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are of difficult healing, and there is nothing but hard work and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come up to the place I have said, and you have faith in the cure,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it clearly, take a tent of bronze or iron, since the fistula is straight, and pierce it.
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is twisted, search for a thin sheet of lead.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for the lead bends easily around its twists.
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot search it well with a needle,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	then cleanse it through one of its openings.
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the liquid flows from one opening to another and cleanses it.
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then pierce it with a sharp instrument as far as your skill allows, to see if there are bones or nerves and if it is completely healed.
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the sick person well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it.
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and once you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, then bind it according to what I have told you.
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and remove the hardened flesh and corrupted matter that are inside.
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed.
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is very deep from a good place, then bind it deeply, as far as you can.
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put in moistened threads with medicinal glue, and insert them right up to the head of the fistula.
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	so that the medicine eats away the superfluity that remains at the bottom.
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put in salves of fresh flesh, until they are healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if they are not healed by that, then cauterize them as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then remove it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If a vein or nerve troubles you or your main members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then scrape it away until all corruption is removed.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with gentle salves as long as necessary until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it does not heal and becomes closed again like before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet at the root of the problem.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	then uncover and search until you reach to the bottom.
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and remove all the corruption, then repair the place.
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep and you cannot reach it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	there is no other remedy than to give in to its natural course.
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small corrupted bone and you can grasp it with pincers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	then extract it with an instrument suitable for that purpose.
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many bones, then remove them all together, not leaving any behind.
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if the liquid opposes you and does not allow for error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	then pierce and release the liquid and the flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then cover the wound with a soothing salve to prevent corruption.
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it like that until the place around the bones is corrupted.
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then they will be more easily removed.
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as the thigh or shinbone,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	then scrape away only the corruption until all blackness is removed.
puis restoure la plaie;	then repair the wound.
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is a large part of it that has corrupted and comes close to the bone marrow,
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	If it needs to be sewn and covered all the way to the corruption, then heal it as long as it is sewed.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about an ulcer that happened to him, i.e., a boil in his leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	if you would take note of the example and help in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man, around 30 years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	as long as the materials came to the leg and it was covered by a large abscess, and had no outward sign for it to open.
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctors through their foolishness closed it so much that the abscess opened up,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and they drained a lot of material, and it became an ulcer, and there came out many fistulas that all went down and moist from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many doctors put a treatment around 2 years, and there was no one wise in the art of hands,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	as long as I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what was draining through the fistulas was of great mass;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the body of the young man became red and had a yellowish orange color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I put a tent in one of the fistulas, and then searched all the fistulas,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that they were coming from each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hurried then, and cut into one of the fistulas as far as I could until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it to be rotten and perforated, and the rot was going all the way down to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what was appearing from the rotten bone, and I thought there wouldn't be any other corruption, except for that which I had already taken out;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with suitable medications over a long time, and it could not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I tried again, and I found the bone just as I had seen it before.
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found that the rot continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then took it out, and I made an effort to close the place.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I couldn't do it until I cut around about the length of a palm of bone, and then I trimmed it so that it was as smooth as all its surface.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medications, and it became sound and healed quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and it was not necessary to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure,
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For often he would bleed out through evacuation, but he was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and instead of the bone a hard flesh grew, and he was in good condition and had no harm or contraindication at all, nor to eat nor to come.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be set like this:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take a string and bind it to the head of the bone that is open,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and take another string of linen larger than the first string, and bind it above the flesh that is over the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the head so that you bring the corrupted flesh down below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh on the place where you see to set it, so that it does not wound the flesh;
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and put a hot ember or a heated iron below the bone to melt and cover the corrupted flesh,
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to set it as long as one can see and feel the corruption, and then set it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of the bone,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh, then put a hot ember below,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then set on fire from one part to the other the corruption, and let it be well charred like a pot, as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, cut out the corrupted joint and set the bone on fire where it contains from the other side;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the joining of the two joints, there is no other remedy than to cut it off.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the wrist of the foot, it is very serious indeed.
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you should investigate that corruption, how it appears to you;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and clean it out in every way that you can, but without causing harm to the tendon or nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and the hot irons to cut these bones are many, according to the size of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and because of this it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each kind of work according to its appearance.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the task itself will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the symptoms of the diseases.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument which you need, according to what is necessary.
dou feu	from fire (i.e. a hot iron or ember)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The eyes can be injured either from inside or from outside (i.e. by injury to the eyeball itself or by burns or other external trauma).
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated that corruption with medicinal remedies and they do not help;
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	then it is necessary to cut off that member up to the point where the corruption comes.
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the disease escapes through amputation from death or from the evil which is more great, namely the loss of the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are that the member becomes black, as if it had been burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and then after the blackness has passed, the corruption of the member spreads from member to member.
