et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes hold all over the body; so hasten to cut (it off).
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if it is by the bite of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones,
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corruption is in the head of the arm, cut it off, and do not give him any time to come down to his hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, cut it off at the wrist, so that the corruption does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes up to the arm, cut it off at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, that's death (i.e. mortal).
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy worse than the quantity of his virtue (i.e. the severity of the disease is so great that it cannot be cured).
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and do likewise when the corruption comes to the foot; if it comes to the first joint, cut off after the second joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes on the foot, cut off the whole foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it ascends to the thigh, cut at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to let the sick person die.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of cutting or burning the member is that you bind it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and extend a servant (i.e. a cord or strap) one end downwards, and another servant the other end upwards.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you will separate the flesh that is between the two cords by one span's length, so that the bone be uncovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then cut or burn (the infected flesh), and put a piece of linen cloth on each side, so that the burning does not touch the healthy place.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and come to the sick person another wound and a swelling which is red (i.e. a purulent infection or abscess).
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if bleeding comes from the incision when you are working, cauterize the place immediately.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or put on some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a convenient cord, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one of my feet in summer: (i.e. this is the beginning of a story about an experience the author had)
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he got a blackness that seemed like it was burned by fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corruption came first to the head of his foot, and it spread all over the foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cut off the foot, and was healed (i.e. cured).
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corruption came back to the head of his hand, and he came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put him on remedies that were supposed to be effective after cleansing the body, but the corruption did not cease;
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of recovering the matter (i.e. curing him).
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted that if I amputated his hand, he would die;
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	because the man's strength was weak, and he completely lost hope, and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and then he hastened to have his hand cut off, and was healed (i.e. cured).
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I tell you this, worse than all other evils, is the one we do when it's necessary to cut off another part (i.e. a more serious amputation).
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Sometimes an abscess comes up in a fleshy place, and stays for so long that it makes a large gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then it rots and bursts, and the pus spatters out, and the place remains empty, just like a vessel that has been emptied.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is just as thin as a delicate silk cloth.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and it does not spread up to the bone, nor up to the nerve, and diseases of this kind are called "boils".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and they are not called a "fistula" (i.e. an abnormal connection between two epithelial-lined surfaces).
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes up to the bone in depth, then it is called a "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the cure is that you cut off all around that skin, and also when it is as thin as a cloth.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and it is not cured by its own corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in depth,
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is thick with flesh, then cure it with a poultice (clister) in this way:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	take note if the breast is large and the abscess that comes out of it has a foul odor.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then apply the poultice made from Egyptian medicine, which is as follows: (i.e. this is where the recipe for the poultice is going to be described)
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take assafoetida, oil, and lye (litarge), in equal parts, and put the mixture into a vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red and becomes as thick as honey.
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take from it according to your need, and make it into a liquid mixture with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and poultice the breast, and bind up the abscess.
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and let the medicine stay on for two hours, then squeeze it out (i.e. remove the poultice).
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the breast is cleansed and free from pus.
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and sometimes it is poulticed with ash water (i.e. a liquid made from the ashes of plants).
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not available, and you take the ashes of grapevine wood, and pour water over them.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it cool, and poultice with it, until you know that the breast is well cleansed.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the sick person cannot bear it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor ash water,
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then poultice with a mixture of water and honey, or add a little lye (litarge) to it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or poultice with a mixture of honey and sweet wine, since honey has the property to cleanse and wash.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the boil heal.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleansed,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then poultice with what brings fresh flesh into it. (i.e. a nourishing or healing substance)
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and take diaphrenetic plaster and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or poultice with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have mentioned or how to make ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the abscess of the breast is small, and the poultice cannot enter into it,
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	then widen it a little with a hot iron, and put inside a tent made of Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, then sew it up and leave only a small space where the poultice can enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the abscess that spatters pus is above (i.e. not directly over the wound), then cut or lower it so that it is over the wound.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Because when the pus is deep, it does not let fresh flesh grow in there.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut off the breast from below as you see fit,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	then arrange it in such a way that the pus runs down to the lowest point.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	because when the pus is deep, it does not let fresh flesh grow in there. (this phrase seems to be repeated from earlier)
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cut off the breast from below as you see fit, then...
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so arrange it in such a way that the pus flows easily downwards, and does not allow any of the pus to remain.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast. (i.e. to help consolidate or solidify the tissue)
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and bind it up with a linen cloth that covers the whole breast.
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cut away at the strongest part of the abscess on the breast, making a cut that is one piece larger than the first.
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then bind sweet ointment over it with another cloth according to the size of the abscess.
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and put it on top of the breast abscess to lighten the pus, and do not take off the large cloth until after several days have passed once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that one which is over the breast abscess, remove often to remove the pus.
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes out of the pus, if it's venom or blood or enough or digestible or indigestible.
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take note if the patient feels pain or not, and whether there is an abscess or not.
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the kind of thing that comes out on top of the breast abscess,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	then know that the breast is healed, and approach the patient's health.
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then unbind him in the morning, or on the third day, and when you take off the bandage,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	you change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast spatters indigestible pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle venom flows out after a long time, then do not lose hope for health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	because good health is approaching. For there are men in whom flesh grows slowly into their wounds, and those who do the opposite (i.e. whose bodies reject new tissue).
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if indigestible pus comes out of the breast after many days, know that the breast has not healed. (this phrase seems to be repeated from earlier)
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breast takes a long time to heal and is inflamed, then apply wet medicine in terms of its substance and dry medicine in terms of its virtue. (i.e. use substances that are moist or liquid on the surface, but have drying properties)
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	such as diaphrenetic ointment, because it has a great part of vitriol in it, and it is the last resort medicine. (i.e. a strong, drying medicine that is used when other treatments have failed)
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take diaphrenetic ointment and mix it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine in equal parts (i.e. in terms of their proportion).
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and do the same with thickened honey, cooked and grown old. (i.e. a mixture of diaphrenetic ointment and honey)
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when diaphrenetic ointment is not available,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, and pound them together, and sprinkle the powder on the honey when it is over the fire.
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then dip a cloth into it, and bind it onto the breast, and at no time apply it with an Aristolgan (a type of bandage or splint) that is too long.
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and the roots of lily of heaven, which are also like flour from flax and centaury (i.e. a plant with medicinal properties).
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use them as simples or compounded ones: pound them together and make a powder, and mix it with the honey that I have mentioned, and use it.
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that the corruption is deep in, and has pressed into the bone, or hard members, or ligaments. (i.e. it has caused serious damage to the underlying tissue)
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	if the treatment of this treatment is a fistula, just as we have said before. (i.e. if the original wound or abscess has become a persistent fistula, then treat it in the same way)
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil on the arm (ungle).
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Panniculus is a boil that grows under the elbow of the pocket of the hand. (i.e. a type of abscess or boil that forms in this specific location)
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or on the foot, or perhaps it comes to be in other places.
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it grows old and one does not take care of it, then a severe boil (aposteme chaus) comes to be there.
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and it spreads and spatters pus as far as the root of the elbow, and perhaps spreads all over. (i.e. the boil or abscess grows and spreads to surrounding tissues)
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and it comes to a corruption so deep that it reaches the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the swelling of the thumb is large, and the color is dark red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not bring any benefit,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	then it is necessary that you cut out all the remaining superfluity which remains of the boil, with an iron tool. (i.e. to remove all remaining tissue or debris from the wound)
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great aid when the bone is healthy and the elbow joint is sound. (i.e. if the underlying bone and joint are healthy, then cauterization can be an effective treatment)
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the elbow joint starts to grow flesh in it, begins to swell and becomes ulcerated. (i.e. the wound or abscess is not healing properly)
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	then it is necessary that you put a splint under the elbow where the flesh is forming.
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it up tight, and carefully cut out that delicate flesh. (i.e. to prevent further growth of the new tissue and allow the wound to heal)
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh caustic and corrosive medicines to remove it all. (i.e. to burn away any remaining tissue that is not healthy)
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it out, and treat the wound with a strong cure, because as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal.
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the thumb corrupting, then cut it off in one piece just like it was said before. (i.e. to amputate the affected part)
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed.
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is festering and suppurating, and it causes great pain, then it is necessary that you cleanse it first. (i.e. to clean out the pus and debris before attempting to heal the wound)
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut off the elbow of the spatula in a crosswise manner on top, (i.e. to amputate the affected part of the arm at the level of the shoulder or upper arm)
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh under the elbow, because the sick person would feel too great pain. (i.e. to avoid cutting into a sensitive area)
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then apply something that soothes. (i.e. to calm and comfort the patient after the procedure)
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of deafness in the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The fingers swell up in some men's hands by chance are entirely fleshy, (i.e. have an excessive amount of flesh or tissue)
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and perhaps it has a joint or bone there, and at no time is it a finger. (i.e. the swelling can be located in different parts of the hand, including joints or bones)
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and some of them come out at the root of the joint, or their birthplace is in certain fingers of the hand. (i.e. the swelling can be located near the joints or fingers)
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	Those that grow on any part of the thumb do not become mute, (i.e. they are not related to deafness)
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and those that grow at the joint of the thumb, by chance become mute. (i.e. they can be associated with deafness)
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cut of him who is fleshy is light, in this way: (i.e. the procedure to remove excess flesh or tissue is relatively simple)
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it out at its root with a wide spatula. (i.e. the surgical procedure to remove the affected tissue is relatively straightforward)
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow at the root of the joint are difficult to cure, if you take it upon yourself to cut. (i.e. the procedure to remove the affected tissue is complex and requires careful consideration)
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	When it grows in or around the back part of the finger, it is necessary that you cut away the surrounding flesh up to the bone first. (i.e. to remove any excess tissue and expose the underlying bone)
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then bind the bone with a suitable thread or cord to it, then dress the wound until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come to the bones in the joints occur by birth, or from a wound, or from being burned with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	Then you must bind that wound, so that it may repair itself according to its natural shape;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two moist cloths or towels dipped in rose oil, so that they do not become stiff.
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of cloth, until the place is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a wound comes to any of his knees with the palm, then bind that wound in the same way.
Des vils	The boils
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	They are foul-smelling, large, swollen and full of melancholy pus, which come on one or more members of the body.
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and they are more likely to occur in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to them an occasional purging with vinegar, and then salve with the oil of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The treatment of iron wounds is in two ways: one is to bind them and draw out the black blood.
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other way is that you lift up the boil, and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The cutting of a boil is done in this way: first, take the leg of a hot iron very firmly, until the thick blood is thinned.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then apply the heated iron to the patient's leg from above the knee all the way down to the part below the kneecap.
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cut the boil in one place, or in two places, or in three, with a wide cut.
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift it up and drain out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, until as much of the bad stuff comes out as the patient can stand.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then bind it and command that he eat meat in anointing black vinegar;
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and repeat the evacuation and salving when the boils are full-grown and painful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The removal of eczema is done in this way: take away the hair from the patient's leg, if there is a lot of it.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put him in a bath and heat the leg with hot water until it becomes red and inflames the boils.
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat him up with the fire and then cut in the length of the boil on the long part of the kneecap or in the area below the ankle.
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then burn the skin with an iron and scrape out the boil from each side until it appears when you feel it.
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and then you see it red and black, and when it enters into the skin it seems as white as a string.
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then apply oil to the boil, so that it is raised out of the skin, and then scrape it with a light iron.
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cut it in another place on top of the three days, then scrape off the skin over the boil until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then apply oil to the boil, just like you did before, and scrape it with another iron, just like you did the first time.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then cut another piece or more if you need to, then apply oil and scrape it at the toe of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then drain and scrape it all the way to the second cut, then pull out piece by piece until it comes out completely, and then cut it.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot drain and scrape it, then insert a needle into every strong thread, double it. (This is likely referring to sewing up the wound with sutures)
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and bind and drain it, and insert a thread under one string, and turn your hand from one side to the other until it comes out. (This is likely referring to suturing the wound shut)
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and take care that it doesn't cut, because if it does, then you can't drain or scrape it out, and it will come to harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drained it all out, then put moist wool soaked in wine and rosated oil on the wound's location, and care for him until he is healed. (Note: "rosated" likely means scented or perfumed)
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and rolled up together, and it's not straight, as we have said... (This sentence seems to be a transition or introduction to another section of the text)
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	it is good that you cut it awry, but do not cut it off completely; and drain it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The form of the iron used to cut the vein is curved, and does not slice, so that it only cuts the boil;
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of thick curve, because if it were fine and subtle, it would cut the vein, but it is thick as we have said, and this is its shape.
De la voinne civile	The boil from which comes pus
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This boil is inflamed in the legs, in hot areas where herbs or trees do not grow, and in dry land.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and it may also occur elsewhere than the legs, and this happens from the filth that comes from under the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	just as it comes from within the body snakes and worms inflamed between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this boil is that it comes to the leg a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the place changes and the boil begins to come out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the pus appears, you should wrap it around with a cloth of linen from 3 to 1 and half until 2 times 3, and tie it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the cloth on the leg, and every time it is full of pus again, wrap it around the cloth and tie it.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, cut off a part and wrap up the remaining one, and do not cut it at its root until it is completely out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it goes back into the flesh and brings about an abscess and filth or putridness in the place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	because of this reason it is good that she be treated little by little all the way up to the top, and that nothing remain in her body. (Note: "elle" refers to a woman or person with a boil)
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this boil when it is treated becomes as long as 5 palms or even 10. (Note: "paume" is an old French unit of measurement, approximately equal to the length of a human hand)
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once an old man came to me, whose it exited 10 palms long, and when you cut it, a thread or pus comes out, and it pierces all the way down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	so that everything comes out; and the matter inside be emptied, and apply to the place medicines against putridness every day, then care for it just like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes this boil has many roots, and especially when it appears in the joint of the foot or the foot itself.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and there comes out much pus, and from which many roots come out; then care for it just as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "bovine sickness", because it has often occurred among oxen.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes up and down through the whole body.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and one feels it very well as it moves from member to member, until it reaches the skin and bursts out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and it is inflamed from putridity of certain humors, such as come from worms and snakes and lice and ascarids or from the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts about its evilness, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; and this has happened many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being cured and drained, one can hardly tell that it was there:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it is good that you bind the area above and below with a strong thread tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut on top and drain outwards, and if the worm is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize with fire above, until it blackens.
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it corrupts the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming near the head close to the eye, then bind a thread under it in a circle, then cut on top and drain outwards.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is good to use the sick person with purifying medicines for the putrid humors, to cleanse the body.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and abstain from meat that causes putrefaction.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness or flatulence.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and after a little while, the vein rose up like a worm to the shoulder.
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	sooner than anything, just as quicksilver when it runs from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain departs from that place and settles in the shoulder.
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then after a little while it ran through the whole body, so that it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	and then she told me that it was turning around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had often heard that the pain could move from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it like this, as I did in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman's body was dry and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and that is why the windiness appeared to be constrained.
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear in this way among those who are luscious and have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see the disease being cured, and the sick person feels that pain, if they show you as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then bind above and below hastily, and then cut on top until the windiness constrained in that place comes out.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you cannot see it to yourself,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then treat with those things that drive out windiness, such as stinking pills and viper pills and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of the splinters or thorns that have entered into the body.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are those with large points and small ones, and thorny, and splintered.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two edges, and those with tongues, and those that have fragments.
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that lodges in any member lodges in either of two ways: or it lodges in a main member, and becomes lodged there.
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as the brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it lodges in any of these parts, and the sign of death that I will tell you about later becomes apparent:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is good that you beware of extracting this splinter, because death comes after in various dispositions.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and if these bad signs do not appear to you, and the splinter is not too deep, then take it out and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain is when the splinter lodges there and pierces the bone, and a sudden convulsion comes out from which is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	is when there is a sudden and violent convulsion, and the face becomes red and swollen, and the tongue is inflamed and red, and there are spasms and disturbances of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps it bursts out from the nostrils or ears; and perhaps it causes loss of speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and there comes out from the wound a moist white discharge, similar to pus, and also like the flesh of burned meat.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if these signs appear, then hold off from treating it, and do not take out the splinter unless it is necessary.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The signs of the spleen when it lodges in the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and feels like it was stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and perhaps the spleen also moves like pus, and there is black bleeding, and a coldness and a cold sweat, and fainting.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then know without doubt that death is near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the splinter when it lodges in the liver is that bloody foam bursts out from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and gasps for breath and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the splinter lodges in the covering of the stomach, it is near the small ribs; and causes great pain and great distress, and gasping for breath; and makes all the muscles of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter lodges in the stomach, perhaps something that is undigested meat comes out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the splinter lodges in the belly and comes out through the intestine without any signs of digestion, then there is no hope for a cure or for extracting the splinter.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the splinter lodges in the bladder and causes the urine to come out and flow away, and the sick person feels a great pain, then know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and forearms and calves and legs and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in a nerve or artery and it is venomous, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to a man who had a splinter lodged in the nerve of his eye, at the root of his neck.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and pulled it out from the other side, under the fat of the ear, and he was cured without any further harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out a splinter that had lodged in the fatty part of the eye, under the paper-thin membrane.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the splinter was closed up and I could only feel the tip towards the surface.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	and the splinter was as thick as a Turkish archer's bowstring, and all the way from one ear to the other; the boy was cured, and no bad accident came of it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I pulled out a splinter from the throat of a Christian, and the splinter was as thick as an Arabian arrowhead at the ears.
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I extracted the barbs and smoothed it out as much as I could, until I was able to pull it out, and the Christian was cured.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And I pulled out a splinter from a man whose spleen had burst open in his stomach, and who thought he was going to die.
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then that it had been thirty days since the event, he did not change his condition;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the splinter and extracted it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And I saw a man whose splinter had lodged in his back, and the wound was already closed over it.
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and the splinter remained inside him, and he did not change his natural condition.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of his natural functions.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And I saw another man whose splinter had lodged in his face, and the wound was already closed over it.
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	and remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And I pulled out a splinter from one of the king's servants, who had it lodged in his neck.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and was slightly declining towards the right side, and the splinter was completely closed up.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was called to the cure three days after it had been lodged, and I found that the wound was very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I searched for it with great subtlety, and did not feel it.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and he felt pain and discomfort under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought that it was the tip of the splinter.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put a poultice on the place that attracts and digests, because the place did not become inflamed.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and I could see the place where the splinter was lodged.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I put another poultice on it for seven days, and the wound healed again, and the sick person remained thus for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	so that he felt the splinter one day inside his neck, and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put on the wound a corrosive remedy for seven days, until it was fully open,
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried to pull it out, and I felt the head of the splinter which had hardened at the place.
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that corrosive remedy until the end of the splinter appeared visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and the tip passed well around four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	and then I enlarged the wound so that I put tongs into it, and pulled on both ends, and it could not come out.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	then I did not stop subtlety and cleverness with instruments, until I was able to take it out one day with well-made tongs.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	according to what its form will come at the end of this chapter, so that I pulled it out and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And the sages judged that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	I was able to restore it then, and the wound was healed, and the sick person was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Now I have told you the quality of extracting some splinters.
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you put your care on what I did not say, for books cannot possibly cover everything.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	But wise masters first consider a small thing, and what is present and failing.
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	understand the work, and new instruments, for the descent of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that needles do not come out of members or are stuck there other than two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by the place where they enter, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out to the other side where it enters is a needle entering into fleshy places and jumping out once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump now, then leave it so long as the flesh is porous around, and loosen the exit;
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	and also if it is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, then leave it so for some days, and move it each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	and then it jumps out, and if it does not jump out, then pierce around with a very fine needle, so that the place around becomes enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the needle is stuck in the bone of the head, and goes up to one of the brains' vents;
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and some of the accidents that I said will appear to the sick person: do not pull it out at all, but leave it so long as it becomes equal after a few days;
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	because if the needle comes up to the brain's ventricle, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the needle is stuck only in the bone and does not come up to the brain,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains the sick person for a few days without bad accident, if one engages with pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck in there and cannot come out, then apply hot poultices around, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the needle has been put back into the body's flesh so that one cannot see it, then search for it in every tent,
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you find it, then pull it out with any convenient instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the needle,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone or nerve or vein in it, then cut so that the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the needle if you can, and if there are ears on the needle where it is stuck.
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	so cut away the flesh that is stuck to both sides of the needle that you can reach;
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the needle, so that you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	and be careful not to break the needle, so that you will pull it out more smoothly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot get it out at once, leave it until the area around the wound is purged, then pull it out, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the hemorrhaging of blood causes contrariety, then administer what we have said about treatment in its chapter.
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and take care of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and make arrangements as you can to pull out the needle without danger.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the sick person in the form that he was in when the needle fell into him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	for it is the greatest aid that he be so, and if you cannot, put him in the form that the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The needle that comes out from another place, where it appears some part of it or the skin is swollen in the area if one can see or feel it apparently:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	cut then above, so that the tweezers can take hold of it, and then pull it out: if it jumps out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, so that it goes into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it still for a bit, and then start the extraction again until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if there is an end of the needle in there, push the rest of the needle into it all the way.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if the end comes out and you can administer warmth, then administer one instrument that is hot.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the needle goes into the hair of the instrument, and then push it out.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the needle is stuck, then insert one instrument with an entering point into it, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the needle is stuck together, then it is suitable that you cut out all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then treat the wound as befits.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the needle has gone into the back or side or belly or bladder or ribcage and is close, and you can cut above it, then cut.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, pull out the needle, and then sew up the wound, if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers with which one pulls out needles are like the beak of a bird, and see here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of it: great, small, and little ones, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the end of the bow string is also like the feather of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	in order to put at the tip of the arrow, as it is this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pliers in order to bend and test if this is so:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the strings of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of strings by which one is tuned are 31, of which it has or head 16.
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	that is to say: 2 bridges that are after the ears, which are called the "herbech".
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the 2 strings which are in 2 apparent temples
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and 2 strings that are in 2 arms of the 2 holes, which are called "aspires".
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	and the string that is through the forehead; and the string that is at the head of the neck.
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the 2 pegs that are in the neck.
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the 2 strings that are on the upper lips above the mouth, and they are called "augeherich".
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and 2 strings that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The strings by which one is commonly tuned are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cerebral, and it is of the left side, and they call it the people "string of the head".
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the middle one is called "faste", and it is composed of the cerebral and the basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	and they call it the people "string of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	and they call it the common people "string of the belly", and it is above the forearm.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and that's the one by which we tune, which appears clearly over the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the Salvadelle is the string that is between the ring and the little finger, and it has 2 branches.
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and in the leg and at the foot are 3 strings: one is under the flap of the left sock,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	and the second one is the Sophène which is at the ankle of the right side; and the string that is called "nèsse", which is at the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	and in the other leg are 3 strings under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The tuning of the strings that are after the ears helps the ancient musicians and people with migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	and the quality of the tune, as I tell you, is that it raises the head of the afflicted person.
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the neck or the strings with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's scarf like a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	Until the two veins appear behind the ears, in two little places dependent on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	and then you feel the pulse under your ear, if it seems to beat;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the lancet and push it under the vein down to the bone, then lift your hand up along the whole vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	and cut and the skin and the vein right in two parts of the crossing, and let out blood until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then bind it tightly so that it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already said the incision and the cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The veins of the two arteries that are in the two temples, so it's worth to remove the old headache;
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and sutures, and accustomed ophthalmia, and in the body of sharp tears with them;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the quality of the surgeon is so as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it's that the patients bind their neck so tightly until the two veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse under your ear, and then they see it beating;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	then lift the skin up on the vein above your index finger to the ear, and push the lancet under.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift up the vein, and cut it, just like you did with the two other veins, and let out blood as needed.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then unbind the patient, and put your finger on top of the vein for an hour, then put a cotton on top;
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	and then bind it firmly and leave it until it's healed; and now I have spoken of their cutting and extraction, in the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The vein in the forehead is so valuable like the saphenous vein for diseases of the face old and with headache and with redness.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	and its quality is that the patients bind their neck in twisting until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	and put the point on the vein, and lift up with your hand or something else, and let out blood as much as you see fit;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then unbind the patient's neck and bind the vein tightly until it is healed, and in no case leave a wide scar.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not good that the scars be too sharp; and the veins are crooked, because the bone is close, and perhaps the scar will break through when it becomes thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The vein of the two arteries that are in the two temples helps with their diseases, and with jaundice, and with redness, and with the ulcer in the eye, and with face diseases.
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	and the quality of their vein is that the patients bind their neck in twisting from any ligature, just as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	then let it heal, and the scar of the transverse vein is one part long of the length of the scar, and one part wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the scar is thin, it may break through; then let out blood as much as you need to, and then bind with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The vein of the neck's vein is so valuable for ague, and for tertian fever, and for face diseases.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	such as headache and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the qualities of the remedy are such that the patient will strain their neck, then strain their navel to your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle flame long, and place it in the middle of the upper lip between the two nostrils.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the vein will not appear well yet, and the pain will now begin to subside.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	and do not go too deep, and make the blood dry up according to your necessity, then leave it one night, for it is very soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The remedy for the two gouty knees helps to tighten the joint, and to begin healing, and to cure many diseases, and to atrophy, and to corrupt, and to herpetic ulcers, and carbuncles.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	and the qualities of the remedy are such that the patient will strain their neck in both ways, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	and let the master be above the head of the sick person, and the sick person sit on one bench.
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then bleed the vein of the long one a little widely, then take out the blood temperately, or as much as is necessary.
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the other part in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and let the veins bleed moderately.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the sick person does not strangle; and let it be until morning, so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	The remedy for the lips.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins on the upper lips helps to cool the mouth and corrupt the gums, and split the lips, and cause the nose to bleed inward.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of the bleeding is to have the patient sit in front of you, and strain their neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, of which one is on the right upper lip and the other on the left upper lip.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the fact that around them there are small dark veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	so cut one and the other, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	so cut the largest one from each side, and do likewise with the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same manner.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the bleeding from the jugular vein, and it's for the constriction of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	and the quality of the person bleeding is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts up their tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	so cut one and the other, and do not go too deep, because under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two manners:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	either with a great and sharp lancet, or a small and subtle one like olive shoots, and it is called "anasil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	and they are great and subtle according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the lancet is very well known, and it's large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	And it needs to be used to open the thick, flat veins that contain much visible blood and are troubled.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of the olive lancet:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it's more delicate and pointed, and it's for bleeding the small veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The bleeding of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	and it is necessary for the bleeder to bleed with caution, and to beware of the artery that is under.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if he cuts the artery, and a great quantity of blood comes out, it is necessary for him to cauterize, as I have said;
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and he should not sharpen the lancet, but shape it like a small olive lancet.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica vein does not open clearly, it is necessary to tie it off and switch to another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you want a drop from it, or you bleed in its place the vein in the arm: it opens clearly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	and cut it with the olive lancet, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you want to know the place of the bleeding, it is necessary then that you tie up the arm, so that you touch the place as long as you know the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the spot with ink, and then tie up the arm, and cut the vein with the olive lancet.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and beware that you do not hit the artery when you see the spot swollen, for it is the artery; then draw back.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it come out high like a child's urine, and the blood is red and subtle, know that it is arterial blood:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	hurry then, and raise your hand up high, then take back your hand if the bleeding stops, as many times has happened;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	tie up the arm, and let it be so, and don't move it until the patient is healed. And may God protect him, and not stir him until he is cured.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.
