And if the blood doesn't stop and it's bothering you, and you don't have any medicine, then cut the artery if it shows itself, because the head of it is retracted; and cauterize the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a scab of fig tree sap, and cut it, and take one half and tie up well right to the other end.
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If the wound is stopped, it's good; if not, then let him take care of it, as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the stopping of the bleeding is not always strong in many conditions for the small size of the wound and the weakness of the arm's ligament.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The bleeding of the vein in the middle helps to treat blood from the head above and the body below;
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said.
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the bleeder to beware of the nerve that is under, and if he goes too deep, he will find the nerve.
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it swells up and the healing becomes weak, and by chance it cannot be healed.
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	and this nerve shows itself many times, and if it doesn't show itself in some people because of its subtlety, then you must bleed with the olive lancet; and draw back from the nerve as far as your power allows.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The bleeding of the cephalic vein helps to treat blood from the head, and helps themselves;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	and it is necessary to bleed with a sharp olive lancet or a sharp myrtle lancet, because it is the safest of all veins, because there is no nerve nor artery underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	However, it is necessary to seek out the lightest spot first, and not to hurt anything if you miss the first time, and then try again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	and by chance the spot swells in some people when you miss the first time, but it doesn't hurt anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you must know about bleeding, is that bleeding is not done except for the sake of preserving health.
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid illnesses from coming;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are outside: namely, the cephalic, the superficial, and the basilica.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	and it should be bled in the beginning of spring, and in autumn, and in winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear.
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	and it should be bled on the first day or on the third day, after two hours or three of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding for illnesses has no fixed hour determined, but when there is need of day or night, in all hours and at all times.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	and it does not seem necessary to bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women who have been pregnant for less than seven months.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly be bled who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to bleed themselves, in whatever manner it may be, they should first cleanse the bowels with a light clyster.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has much foul matter retained, so that the veins will not draw out the superfluities and bad things from the principal members.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	nor should one bleed those who are too full of meats, or drunk, as long as they remain so, nor dropsical.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and beware of bleeding after passionate colic, and vomiting, and purging of the belly, and multiplicity of coition with women, and labor, wakefulness, and fatigue, and all that pertains to virtue, or by cause of the arm or body.
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then subtly purge the humors, if the blood is thick, with meats and drinks and medications, if you have the power;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	then take an emetic or a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtlety cleanse the blood.
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	and bleed from the vein of the liver around the third time, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	and keep that day free from work, and pain, and luxury, and similar things.
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	and be joyful and glad, and have the bleeder sit higher than the one being bled, and apply a cloth to the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	then stretch the ligature above moderately, because if it is too tight or loose, it cannot stop the bleeding.
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	and then rub the area with hands until the veins swell and are felt again.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	then moisten the bleeder's hand with a sharp flame from an old oil flask, then place their right fist over the vein below the area where they are to be bled.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burst and tear when being pricked.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that burst as readily as strings do to the bleeder, and some of them are so full of windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	so that when one puts the flame on it, it recoils from the flame, and cannot be opened by the bleeder, and thus is one of them.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	and if he has opened the vein, then the wound is too narrow, therefore it is necessary for the bleeder to be warned in these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened on the first try, that's good; but if not, he should start again quickly, near or above that spot, if the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is swollen and the sickness worsens, then let it be left alone for a day or two, and do not bind up the arm.
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	by chance there will come abscesses or swellings; don't take a bath, and then try the bleeding again if it pleases them.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the puncture is small or the blood flows subtly and you doubt whether there is as much bleeding as you see, then apply flame to that very same puncture right through.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and it will work a little quickly, even if the area is swollen; for such things often happen when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the area swollen, do not attempt to bleed again, and apply a little linseed oil to it, for it lightens the body of the blood, and is more soothing in this place than the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	and thus administer linseed oil to each bleeding that you do with veins, in order to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	and it also works with onion and garlic juice, when applied to the area; it subtly stops the bleeding and separates it when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if there comes a large abscess, which has often happened when it was not bled in time, or the opening of the vein is small.
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	so hasten and apply a damp sponge to the area in hot water and vinegar for a little while, and then squeeze it out for an hour.
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	and it is necessary to do this after the bleeding from the vein has stopped, and if there remains at the site some darkening or greenish color, it does not harm.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	and if you see any redness, apply some ointment made from aloe or myrrh mixed with camphor, mustard, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there has been an abscess and appearance after the bleeding from the basilica vein: therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to the pressure of the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, beware that you do not apply anything from what we have said, for it may cut short the vein's blood supply; but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then cover it with another dressing until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each bleeding in proportion to its quantity and virtue, and according to the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see a lot of it, let it continue to flow until it becomes more subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And for those who are plethoric and full, and need to be bled, it is necessary to make a larger wound, and to have wider flames.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed them a little and often, and they should be bled by cutting across, not by puncturing.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this manner of bleeding is safe from purging of blood and cutting of nerves, and it is worth more than the bleeding by long or wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for those whose body is weakened by bleeding, it is necessary to give a moist compress made from fresh lemon juice; if they are overheated, treat the blood with three or four treatments.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if they have a cold complexion, mix before the bleeding a moist compress with a sweet syrup or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if they faint at the bleeding, after the blood has flowed out, it is necessary that they sniff a broth made of meat and a subtle, fragrant syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use the other things that we have said in the chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to move his arm and heal another time, so it must be, when it is weakened by great blood loss, that he heals gradually little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to move his arm after the first healing, and he has strong vigor, then it heals within 7 hours after the first healing, or within the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal from another side, then he must heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	For he has much blood inside the body which is already heated up and makes fever; so it must be drained in large quantity, and the wound must be opened wide enough until pus comes out.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then that you reward all the conditions of healing, and put your hand on the pulse when it heals, so that pus does not come in place of healing.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens many times, when the healer is careless;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it does not need to happen again that you want to untie the arm, and let blood out the second time, and the wound is closed, so you press hard on it;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	nor if it's crooked, that he stretches the arm quickly, for that would be bad.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	but leave it alone until it heals the second time; or you go to the tip of the flame, so that the blood which has congealed comes out with pus again.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on 1 pot of oil poured into water, and press on it lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the abscess is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it, until the swelling has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to let out blood the second time, then he heals in that same place, or in another abscess, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The wound on the arm is healed in place of the swelling of the head because it was composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the manner of treatment is such that the patient dips their hand into hot water until it is red.
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then it should be wrapped slightly so that the swelling becomes visible, then heal now through the middle, not through the length or breadth.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and the abscesses should be large, and should be treated well near the joint of the hand, and they cannot come out without it, if you put your hand in hot water, and let the pus stay in the water, as long as you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	and if it is in summer, do not put your hand again in hot water, for you put it more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	and the healing of this wound is safer from all other wounds, than there are arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The cure for the abscess on the right hand is worth all diseases of the liver, and this is how:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	strip the skin, and dip it in hot water, until the abscess becomes inflamed, so that one can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	and if it heals through the middle, and you cut it all out, then nothing hurts.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	and do not go too deep, because the nerves are beneath, stripped of flesh,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then put the hand in hot water, if the pus is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the wound with oil as long as it is needed, then put a compress on the abscess to close it quickly, and do this for each pain. (Note: "hastanment" means "quickly", and "chescun rain" is an archaic way of saying "each time")
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The cure for the abscess in the left hand is worth for the disease of the spleen, and do everything similarly as I told you about the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The cure for the abscess in the groin is worth for all diseases that are under the body. (Note: "sophene" refers to an area of the body, possibly near the navel or lower abdomen)
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as diseases of the kidneys, and retention of fluids, and disease of the intestines, and old legs and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of its cure is that the sick person puts their foot in hot water, and rubs on the abscess until it bursts.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and lies above the ankle joint; and if the abscess is at the ankle, and over the foot, there go many veins.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	cure it then in the largest vein, or the one at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cure it above the foot, then beware of the nerves that are below, and the cure goes through as well when cutting; and the scar will be thin.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the pus cannot come out, then put the foot in water again, and let it drain well from the abscess.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if the treatment fails at first, then start again a second time above a spot, because the place is salty. (Note: "salz" here means that the area has been previously treated and possibly left with a residue or crust)
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	do not doubt about nerves, as we have said, and do the same for the abscess in the other foot as well.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The sore of the sciatic vein is at the ankle of the back leg, and its cure is worth for the pain in the hip, when it's due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the quality of its cure is that the sick person goes to bathe and rubs on top of the ankle with four fingers twisting, turning.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	because otherwise the abscess will not open; and if it does open, then cure it in all ways that you can, and by cutting through.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it's worth more if you cut it, because the sore is deep and it is often reopened for many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't find it, then cure any vein that opens behind the foot, and near to the small toe, and beware of the nerves.
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	and do so much as you can with the bleeding, then loosen the ligature and put on a compress and tie it up tightly; now she is cured.
Des sainies de ventouse	It seems like we're moving to a new section of the text. The phrase "Des sainies de ventouse" can be translated to "Of cures with a ventouse", which refers to a medical instrument used for applying suction or vacuum. Are you ready to read about that?
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or copper, or glass; and ventousation is done in two ways: either by making an incision to draw out blood, or without making an incision.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventousation that is done without cutting is in two ways: either it is done with fire, or without fire. (Note: "a tout feu" means "with the application of heat", likely from a hot iron or similar tool)
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and this ventousation that is done by cutting and drawing out blood is made in 14 places on the body.
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	which one is at the top of the head, and the others are near the neck.
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two more on each side of the neck, and the ventouse under the chin.
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	and the ventouses on the two shoulders, and the ventouses above the ribs.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	and the ventouses in the two arms, and the ventouses in the two legs.
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and the ventouses on the two ankles; and the ventousation does not draw out blood, except from small abscesses that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and for this reason it does no harm, just like treating an abscess with a cure.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it's not suitable that it be administered, with or without fire, in any disease that comes from excess, as long as the whole body is drained.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if due to necessity of disease or habit it's necessary to ventouse, then we should administer each one hour at the beginning or end of the month, and in between and during every season.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	because there are such people who, when they need to be ventoused, have a heavy head. (Note: likely referring to people with a fever or other condition that makes them feel dizzy or lightheaded)
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and there are such people who find swelling and redness in their face, and head, and neck, and darkness in themselves. (Note: "tenebrour" likely refers to a dark or murky complexion)
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and such people who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have swollen lips, and are bleeding.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	and there are such people who dream, and see with their eyes blood and wounds and bites and similar things. (Note: likely referring to vivid or disturbing visualizations in dreams)
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and just the same when it's in the month, we order them to be ventoused after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The cure for the nose is useful for the swelling of the head... that comes from themselves, and it's not suitable to do after the evacuation of all the body. (Note: likely referring to a specific medical treatment or procedure)
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	and this ventousation is in place of the cure for the cephalic vein,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it's not suitable that those with a cold temperament or who have catarrh use it, because it does them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	and for this reason it's not suitable that the elderly use it, nor those who have cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who cure themselves with it often become forgetful, and for this reason the ventouse should be placed a bit lower by the back of the head, in order to counteract forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The ventousation on the neck is in place of the cure for the head and the basilic vein, and for this reason it's worth it for the constriction of the chest.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and for rupture of the channel of the womb, and in the breast, and in excess.
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	and it should be placed a bit lower, because if it is too tightly held, it will cause forgetfulness or nausea and of the heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventousations on the two sides of the neck are worth for headaches, and eye pains (obtalmia) and migraines, and for strangulation, and for pain in the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	and it's in place of the cure for the basilic vein. And you should command the surgeon to express his hand when putting it on, so that he doesn't cut the artery and comes out without drawing any blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventousation under the chin is worth for diseases of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar illnesses that are in the mouth; and it's in place of the cures for the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventousation on the shoulders is worth for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventousation on the sides (costs) is worth as much as three abscesses of the arm.
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	because it draws blood from these large abscesses.
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and command the surgeon not to cut too deeply in it, because the place is bare of flesh and lies near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The ventouse on the backside is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and diseases below, and it's necessary that the ventouse be large and made of copper, so that it can draw well; and perhaps if it were subtle, it would break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouses on the legs are clear in their healing, because they draw blood from the whole body, and are worth for old pains of the reins, and the kidneys, and the bladder, and they clean out the stones; and they replace the two saphene veins, and the two ankle ventouses, but despite this, after long use they weaken the body and bring on a condition of wasting in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the ventouse is that you first put it on empty, and then fill it with air in a temperate manner, and quickly place it on, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the area red and swollen, and observe the redness of the blood; then cut, and reapply the ventouses, and be aware of the condition of the body, because there are such people who have thick flesh and clear pores: so it is necessary to cut only once, and make large and somewhat deep wounds, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it's necessary to cut twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it's necessary to cut a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, it suffices with one single cut.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we want a lot of blood to come out, we should repeat the cuts often; and if the blood is thick, we should cut deeply, and when the end is reached, it's that the knife should be plunged in suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	and it's necessary for those who have thick skin and hard flesh, and who have narrow pores, that you anoint the areas around the ventouses with oil that is appetizing and dissolving.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it's in this state, of violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucumber seed oil.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	and if it's in a yellowish state, of oil of parsley, or lily, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, then take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or aniseed oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the person being treated has tender skin and wide pores, then it's not necessary to put any oil on them.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	but it's necessary to wash afterwards with red wine water, or cold water, or wormwood water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, should rise from ashes, or wormwood water, and sumac, and similar things. (Note: "mout de moistor" likely means someone with a lot of bodily fluids or moisture)
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those who have thick superfluities should rise with old wine, or wormwood water, or a decoction of aniseed or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it's not suitable to treat with a ventouse before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep afterwards.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	and it's necessary that he be warm, both when he is to be ventoused and when he has been ventoused.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And beware of those who treat themselves as choleric people are, and whose blood is too hot and inflamed.
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	so it's necessary that he take cold things, such as unripe grapes and chicories and lettuce on ashes, and similar things.
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and drink vinegar, and meat broth, and damp meats. (Note: "pucins" is likely a reference to some kind of fruit or vegetable, possibly related to apples or plums)
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And those who have a cold temperament, should take honey syrup and medium-smelling wine, which is between old and new, and drink little, and drink vinegar, and drink little fruit, and small birds, such as pigeons. (Note: "odorant moien" likely means wine with a pleasant or moderate smell, rather than one that's very strong)
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and on the day when he will be ventoused, he should drink more than eat.
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	and it's necessary to give some people some tritical or muscat wine before the ventousation, or afterwards, in order to comfort the main limbs. (Note: "tritical" is likely a reference to a type of wine, possibly similar to "muscat", which was known for its medicinal properties)
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	and the blood should be thinned, but it's not necessary for those who are hot to drink it. (Note: in this context, "hot" likely refers to someone with a fever or inflammation, and they would not benefit from drinking blood)
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The ventouses that are placed without cutting are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and the navel and the reins and the groin, because these members do not suffer being cut on them. (Note: in this context, "without cutting" refers to the ventouse being used without making an incision)
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it's only done for drawing blood from member to member. (Note: this suggests that the ventouse is used to transfer blood from one part of the body to another, rather than to drain blood from a specific area)
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	such as when we put them on the shoulders to let blood flow from them; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, such as when we put ventouses on the stomach and on the navel to reduce the size of the member. (Note: "viscositeit" likely refers to a thick or sticky substance, possibly related to fluid buildup or inflammation)
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	and it removes the pain, when there is swelling or bruising; and by its attractive virtue, it may possibly remove the swelling, or drive out the bruise from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	and so does it when it is put on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained windiness. (Note: "ventositeit" likely refers to an accumulation of air or gas in the body, possibly related to digestive issues)
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	and these ventouses are administered empty in order to suck out blood alone; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water. (Note: "feu" likely refers to a heated instrument or substance being used alongside the ventouse)
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	such as in cases of pleurisy, and in this manner the ventouse is filled with hot water or with water that has been boiled herbs which are suitable for this. (Note: "covenaubles" likely means "convenient" or "suitable", and "cuit herbes" refers to herbs that have been cooked or boiled)
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the ventouse administered with fire is this:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two fingers in width and half a palm in depth, and on the side, around the middle, one small hole, such as for sticking an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it's made of copper, smooth so that it doesn't hurt the patient when put on the member.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	and has in the middle a rod crossing from copper or iron, to hold a wick seized. (Note: "chandoile" likely refers to a candle or a flame)
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and there are great and small ones, according to the diseases and the age of those who take them.
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the ventouses for children are different from those for adults, and for thin people from those for fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And so should this ventouse be put on the member:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	ignite the wick with wax or a linen thread, and place it inside the ventouse across the rod that is inside the ventouse.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the ventouse, so that it doesn't burn the patient.
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then put it on the member, and the hands should be on the hole that we mentioned, so that when you want to, the steam comes out and one can remove the ventouse.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and then ignite it again like before, and repeat this several times if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the ventouse that is administered for disease of pleurisy, all water is added, there is no rod nor hole, and it is only administered with fire when it is filled with water, and it is placed on the member alone.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Ventouses are only administered with fire in members where you cannot put ventouses because of their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar areas.
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in places bare of flesh, such as elbows or knees, and others similar.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and the quality of the user is that when you find ventouses that are in soft and clean waters without any sediment, take them.
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and soak them in sweet water, until they are well-known, and have nothing in their bellies.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then let them be cured with wine and a ventouse, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the ventouses.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and firm, if it is a place where you can put a ventouse, then put one there, because this is worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise the place with ashes, and then with water, well done, and then test it. (Note: "espreint" likely means to apply a gentle pressure or to check for tenderness)
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the place heals too slowly from the flesh of the ventouses, moisten a linen cloth in cold water and put it on, until the blood is stopped.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if the blood is multiplied, put on vitriol that has been boiled or gall, and similar things, until it is stopped. (Note: "vitriol" likely refers to a type of acid or corrosive substance)
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you can put on the place half-cooked peeled beans and leave them until they dry out the wound, which will now stop bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other ventouses.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the ventouses won't stick, rub the area with fresh blood or you can insert a needle until the blood comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	and then put them on and as soon as they feel the blood, they will stick.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	and when you see that they are leaking, sprinkle on a little aloes and burnt silk or ashes, so they will now dry up.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	The book of wounds begins here. (Note: this likely marks the end of the section on ventouses and the beginning of a new chapter in the medical text)
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a treatment for wounds and swellings.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know, dear son, that foolish men scorn this chapter, having never seen any of the old books nor read a letter about it.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason is the knowledge estranged in our land, for I have never found any good one.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else, except by the knowledge of the old books, in which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	and I have written in this chapter what is contained, and shortened it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are brought, as I have done in the two chapters before this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say the prologue of this book, which contains the sum of words and chapters where the wise man sets his understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proven know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when any breakage or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to someone, it is necessary that you hasten to cure the ailing person on one hand and, if nothing else is the case, such as weakness of body, or infancy, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	or if the body's temper is very cold or too hot; and in case of cold fever, it means cold juices, such as bird and goat meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat greasy foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have no doubt about a warm abscess or bursting of matter into the member; then let the patient return to his previous treatment right away.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone starts to heal, it is necessary that one nourishes the patient with meats that make thick nourishment, or have viscosity, such as boiled wheat, rice, cheese, and veal, and eggs, and fresh fish, and rich wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with proper nourishment the bone heals more quickly and sooner the breakage.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well reunited or mended according to their natural order because of the weariness of the members, nor those also who are too soft, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	but there is no cure, scrape off on the broken bone, that is to say, large scabs which have formed and joined the member together, as long as it strengthens itself like before; and do not remove them completely, and therefore it is necessary to nourish with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breakages are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the breakage of the head is different from the breakage of the thigh or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that bend (or fracture) at a curve, and others in a crackling manner, such as the breakage of a quill pen for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And also a break with an open wound, and a break with a small crack or fissure throughout its entire length.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And each type has its own remedy and proper instrument in restoration, according to what the memory dictates in its place.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and it is known that a break of the bone by this, that the place is twisted and opens well from outside, and sounds when pressed with the hand.
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	and if there is no twist or sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it can well have a twist, crack, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So you should not move the hand at all, but put on medications that come next, and then bind it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that bends in a curve, and where the two parts are disjointed, it is necessary to bind them now so that they meet equally again, just as if an abscess were to come.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	and if the abscess comes, then leave it alone for a day, until the abscess is calmed down.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then bind it equally to the bandages that you put lightly and gently, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restorations of those where there are splinters; then bind it, as it is necessary next.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, and they extend into two parts, such as hands or feet, or if it is in your hand, then it is a small member, or if it is to two strings, or to one string and your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member are straightened out, scrape off by all means the additions in their places with bandages that you put on, and be careful that through your work no harm or pain comes to the patient.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	and join well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if it seems to you that it is not well, feel it with your hand: straighten it beautifully and do not bind it too tightly or press it, as those who by their work bring about hot abscesses and contraction in the member, which we have warned against many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the member is well-settled, scold the patient that they do not move it, nor in waking nor in sleeping, nor in turning or any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	and take good care that the member is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when it does not feel any pain, then it is not well-settled, and it must be put in such a condition that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and take care that it is set straight, so that there may not be any twisting when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken member is as I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: it is necessary to envelop them in soft and subtle linen cloths.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	and those that are large, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to envelop them in a wide and thick linen cloth, for the broad cloths enclose all the great member and bind it from all sides equally, so that there may be no unevenness.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	then tie the ends of the cloths together with light stitches, three or four turns according to the member, and bind your hand a bit to the whole cloth, then go above the break and bind it less tightly than the break, so that the break may be a bit further away from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	and soften the linen cloth a bit and a bit, until you take up most of the clean part of the wound, then take another cloth and tie it around again on top of the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	then go back to the part below the break and bind it moderately, not too tightly nor too loosely, as we said in the first lesson above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	then put between the linen cloths or bandages as many as it takes to make them all even and flat, then tie everything with one bandage on top, and then put your well-made splints above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then put on something soothing and hot to calm the abscess, and which removes the swelling, and leave it like that for a few days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	then bind the splints above with a strip of wood as thick as a cane, or from the tree where you make shovels, or from palm fronds, and let them be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	but it is necessary that the splint you put on top of the break should be a bit thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and let it be as long as is needed for the member, either small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then bind the splints on top just like you did in the first lesson, and then tie a thread on top gently, just like on the break in the first lesson.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	the tighter it is above, the looser it should be below; and it is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and made of soft linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, like I want from the works of fools who make their stitches with strings of linen cord twisted in knots, and it's a great mistake, because the stitch can't be even if it's too fine, and it shouldn't have more than half a finger width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is cut by the splints after they are tightened in their proper place, then put underneath them linen cloths or lint to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the break and the ligament is broken, I will say how it should be cured later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that you must not bind with splints all the broken members at first.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the members are large, you should not put splints on them until after 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of hot abscess supervening.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	and see here the manner of ancient poultices for restoring breaks, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that is stored in the walls of the mill, and mix it with a lot of egg, and apply this concoction, neither too thin nor too thick, and it's a common way to use a poultice to restore breaks in many cases, especially for women and small children, because it's not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of poultice restoring breaks, dislocations, and torsions: take 3 parts of aloes, gum arabic, myrrh, and bezoar stone, and mix with 10 parts of resin; add 5 parts of mirre and aloe, and 8 parts of alachil; reduce to powder, and mix with plenty of egg. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this poultice, because it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of poultice that is worth for torsion: take myrrh and vernalis, in 10 parts; mirre and aloe, in 8 parts; acacia, in 6 parts; Armenian bolic, in 10 parts. Pound well together, and mix with vinegar or plenty of egg. And administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another manner of poultice for joints and bones that have become dislocated from their place, and calms the pain that may arise, and is used to treat bone fractures: take fresh linen, soak it in warm water and oil, and apply it to the area. These poultices do not restore, but they are good for calming hot abscesses and properly removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of poultice that restores broken bones: take dry leaves of fig tree and dry leaves of wild pomegranate, and pound them together to make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another manner of poultice for the restoration of bone fractures and to soften the remaining abscess. Take equal parts of roots of vernalis, camomile, violet flowers, and farina of oats; pound them together, mix with wine, and if the member is hot, mix with moisted coriander juice or vinegar, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another manner of poultice stronger than the first one, when hard abscesses come to the restoration of the member. Take equal parts of roots of vernalis, and seeds of flax, balaustine, mellilotus, and savin, and flowers of violets and camomile; pound them together, and mix with salted vinegar or sweet vinegar or wine, according to the heat of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that when restoring a broken member, one should only apply ointment made of wax and oil on it, and nothing else, and that it should be between two extremes, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And Galen seems to say that when restoring a broken member, one should apply dry and slightly warm things on it, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, which we have already mentioned.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of poultice that is good for lesions and pain: take myrrh and the hairs from a depilated man or goose feathers, and equal parts of vernalis, and pound them together to make a poultice.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then wait a little while after that, and be careful if the patient feels any pain or if the bone has not returned to its place, do not remove the poultice for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain or itching or swelling comes to the place, or inflammation, hurry and remove it, and take off the poultice immediately. And take a light cloth and a moist sea sponge, dip them in water, and use them to lift up the area, until the itching ceases and the pain is calmed.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	then let the member rest for an hour, and then put on dry linen that is moistened with water or rose oil, and tie it in place with a nut, until you are sure of no hot abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest and be calmed, then resume the fine stitching and a bit of poultice, and do not bind it too tightly as before. And proceed with subtlety until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess and redness and pain and swelling have completely gone away, and you need to continue with poultice and bandage, then start again as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if none of what we have said happens to the member, then do not remove the bandage until after 3 days or 4 or 5 or 7 days, and never for more than 20 days, as long as you see that the break is healing and approaching the union with the flesh on it.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	then the flesh will close more than before, and grow in a healthy way, as I said before. And if you see that the area is drying out more than necessary, know that there can be no pus formation.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	then take the thread of hot water and tear it out every time you remove the bandage, and do this three times a day, and clean the stitching area a little each time.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	through this work you cut away the pus from the member and heal it quickly, and you undo what foolish people do to restore a broken limb in an improper way: it's evil, and it's a poor work, and I see nothing but laziness and doing things wrongly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	It seems like the text is concluding with a heading "des diverses manieres de brisure", which translates to "of various manners of breakage" or "of different types of fractures". This suggests that the author is about to discuss or describe various types of breaks or injuries, possibly in preparation for discussing treatment methods.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many manners of breaks are, and various shapes, and the causes are destined;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	for there are breaks that are made by striking with a sword, and the arm is broken so that it takes all the bone down to the point of the shoulder blade, which is under the bone, just like a hatchet or an axe; and because of this, it is called this manner of break "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone above without piercing it, and is called this manner of break "absolute"; and the wound of these two breaks is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it's a crushing blow, or a splitting break, or from the back of the arm with stone, or falling on stone, or other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it's a comminuted break, which approaches just to the periosteum that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there's a wound that is closed in the bone as fine as a thread, and it's a small crack, and because of this it's called this break "capillary".
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by striking with stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and causes the bone piece to go inward, and it's like the hole that blacksmiths make when they heat up their furnaces, so the stone goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And these things happen more often to those who have soft bones in the head, like infants'.
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and all these manners of breaks have small fragments that are separated like splints; and I will speak about them in their proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breaks by the signs on them, and the investigation that is made, and by the corrupt flesh that is over them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary break is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone and rubs it gently, the break opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, be careful about accidents that can occur in the patient. And if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, swelling, and fever ague, or if they persist and become red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot be healed with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident and you hope for recovery, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes first to you, and it's in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the periosteum under the bone is not corrupted and the accidents we mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the break of the bone comes just to the periosteum that covers the brain, then it is necessary for you to cut through the broken part in this way: take hold of the head of the wounded person and uncover the bone in every way that you can, and on the figure of the wound as softly as you can.
