puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie a cloth around the top of the staff so that it does not touch the patient; and place the staff under the elbow of the patient; extend the staff on the long side, and tie the aid to the staff, and the arm at the end of the hand; then put the arm on one splint of an iron rod as wide, and let the hands be lowered, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will now be restored.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is reduced, however it may be, you should put under the elbow a staff of wool as tall; then place the poultice around with flour powder, with incense and egg oil, on all the shoulder and around, then the strain under the elbow properly, and turn the strap on the poultice, and embrace the hand to his neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he rest a while, as long as the members are comfortable, because it will heal more quickly; and then rest again after 5 days or 7, and move him; and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is inflamed because of too much heat or moisture that has come to it, or for another reason, you should administer cauterization into three punctures, as it is placed before the cauterizer.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and after 7 days the joint comes apart, and it cannot lift its arm up, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place again.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is near the chest or the shoulders or the back, it is made by pushing and stretching of the hands, and administering another type of treatment; and cure until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes grief to the member, and slowly in movement, the patient should bathe many times, until that grief is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	from a dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated to the point, and it returns to the point, and it has been dislocated from all sides, and especially in front and back, and the dislocation is not reset, for one sees it well and feels it well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the sick shoulder with the healthy one, if it can be seen clearly. For the joint is raised, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its own scapula at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you treat it thus before the suppurating sores come, for if the suppurating sores come, it would be painful to reduce it; and possibly it cannot be reduced entirely, especially when it is in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and is of greater pain, and possibly death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is such, when it can be reduced to this, that you stretch out its hand with both of your hands; and its arm is spread, and the hands of the patient according to the shoulder, around and above and below, and push the joint into its own hollows together, or to the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and pushes with the root of his palm the shoulder which is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and do that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two ministers, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from one side to the other, then wrap a double long and wide cloth around.
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the patient has joined the joint to his hand, he should rub it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint firmly, until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	and when it is in its place, he should put on dry poultice with some egg yolk, and bind it firmly, and let the arm hang by the neck of the patient for a while, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, remove the bandage and let it be; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, repeat the poultice and the bandage, and let it be like this for some time, until it is firmly set; then release.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if he feels pain or swelling after the reduction of the joint, and it becomes inflamed, bathe him and gently rub him, and press until it is eased; or put a fat lamb's poultice on the joint, then let it be for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter into the bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the poultice back on, and then have him enter into the bath; and do this two or three times until it is healed; and if you see that it doesn't improve, take moistened cow's hair heated with butter and bind it to the joint; it will return to its normal state.
li dislocation de la main	It seems we've come full circle! The text appears to be a medieval medical treatise on how to treat a dislocated hand or wrist, specifically focusing on reduction techniques and aftercare.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joints of the hand become dislocated, and the return is light, more than other joints Nevertheless, it must be brought back to its place promptly, in the same way that it was dislocated, even if the joint swells or an abscess forms there.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the return is that you place the diseased hand on a table, and extend the members of the hand, and the doctor places it equal, so that he puts his palm on the appearance of the joint, and pushes it until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Nevertheless, you should see if it is well in place; then put the diseased hand with its back on a table at extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, he puts the diseased hand with its back on the table, and the doctor puts his hand on that appearance of the joint. If it now returns, it's good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, he applies a poultice of soothing emplastrum and lets it be so that it doesn't start again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he can't endure it, and you can't put it back in place after some days, the deformed joint remains.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and nothing can harm the sick person except as long as the hand is swollen, and cannot grasp anything at all: then you know that the nerves are torn, or the arteries; if there's no other remedy than to cut around the case and by chance it won't be any worse.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, he puts on the poultice that we have said, then tightens it and leaves it for 5 days, then loosens it and leaves it so.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he can't move it well and there's any stiffness, he soaks the hand in hot water, and rubs it until it is relaxed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	It seems that the text was about treating a specific medical condition, namely "dislocation of the thumb", which is an old-fashioned term for a type of joint injury or dislocation.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	At times the elbow of the hand is dislocated to each side, at times to the back of the palm or to the wrist.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then place the elbow and push the dislocation back into its place as long as it returns, then support the head of the elbow and guide it towards the part where it is joined.

et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	and do the same if it is dislocated at the wrist of the hand, and do what you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same also when it is dislocated in another way.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	from the dislocation of the vertebra of the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra of the back or of the neck is dislocated, or there are several that are dislocated, then there is no remedy, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the evacuations jump out without voluntary intention, and they cannot be held, and many times are softened in some member, or the two thighs or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And often the vertebrae move to four parts; that which moves at the back is called "gyphosis".
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	the remedy is to apply a treatment if the gyphosis has come from childhood: if there is no remedy or healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And that which comes from falling or being struck or similar things, the ancient men said it is a way of treatment by great words, but it does not bring any great benefit.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	but I have shortened it according to my intention, and formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the swelling that comes to the elbow in front, there is no cure nor health.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	and also those that come straight to the two sides, and one cannot cure boils that properly come to the back, as I say;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and that the patient be extended on their face in one equal place and have a strain under them so they do not break.

et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	and two servants know the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two sticks.
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	and be well fastened, the sticks as we have said, and the physician put their palms on the spine firmly, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not recover by this cure, then take a board of three arms long, and sharpen it under the surface, and the patient will be on their side, and put the head of the board under the surface, then place the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and the physician puts their feet on the other end of the board and presses well, until it recovers to its place; and if you see that it cannot be done by this means, then do it with the turning wheel which turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And take two sticks of great length and place one at the head of the patient, and two others towards the feet, with a hand's breadth between each stick, above and below.
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and on each stick have one hole, where the turning wheel fits in, and let the sticks be firmly stuck in the ground so they don't move; and between each pair of sticks there will be a turning rod, with which the patient's body is turned, and on each turning rod there will be two small sticks of a hand's breadth long, to turn the turning wheel.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cord that is between the thighs to the turning wheel towards the head, and the other cord towards the feet to the other turning wheel; and each of the servants will turn their turning wheel in the same direction as the whole cord, and the master will put the spine straight, just as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is straightened, then put on drying plaster with a large amount of egg whites, and then the poultices, and then the straitening board of three fists long, to stretch the place of the sciatic nerve and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a cord, just as we have said, and use subtle nourishing ointments on the patient until they are healed.
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if nothing comes to an end with the healing, it is convenient to administer softening and soothing medicines, along with the straitening board that we have said before; and at no time should one administer more than a piece of linen.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	and at no time should the appearance of protrusion in the lower back of the spine seem like a dislocation, and be mistaken for such, because it is actually the bone that has come out, and one should not have any assumption about this: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	It seems we've reached the end of the text.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Know that dislocations occur only at the joints of the hip and shoulder, but not in the same way as other joints; and the joint of the hip is displaced in four parts: inward and outward, and forward and backward; and more so inward than outward, and it comes forward and backward.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation in this way is that when you join the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee appears more swollen than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot bend their knee.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the lump that is near to the inflamed and hot aposteme, because the veins of the thigh come there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one to whom it happens outward is that this accident is contrary to those in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of the one to whom it happens in front are that they feel well their leg according to completion; however, they do not double up their knee without pain, and if you want them to walk, they cannot go forward, and they retain their urine, and swell the groin, and when they go, they pass above the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of the one to whom it happens in back are that he cannot stretch his knee, nor bend it, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the groin is softened, and the veins of the thigh are at the level of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this resemblance of dislocation are that you return to see if the dislocation is ancient and has remained in its position, then there is no treatment; and it is not necessary to have hope.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in the one whose dislocation is fresh, and this is of four kinds of dislocation, so hasten that you return the joint, and push it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will recover, and there is no need for further treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	And if it does not recover in this way, so it behooves you to get one strong man, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or with one strap that is tied above the knee;
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another strong man extends his hand above in such a manner that he pushes his hands under his buttocks, then tightens one soft cord above the knee; and another ties the top of the cord.
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they pull upwards and downwards all at once, until the sick person is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four appearances, and if the dislocation has recovered, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If this does not happen, it behooves you to put a cure on its appearance. When the dislocation is at the breaking point, it behooves you that you support the sick person on his healthy side, then put the cord on the root of the knee, and the part which is under the bend, then pull the cord up towards the bend, and towards the fleshy part.
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	then take hold of another strong person's arms, and encircle the thick part of the sick knee, and stretch it out to the far end strongly: if it will recover to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot tie it in this manner as we have said, it behooves you to bind the two feet of the sick person together with a strong soft cord above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the sick leg be stretched out two inches more than the other.
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	then it should be hung on the top of a pole, and be above the ground two arms' length; then command one servant to encircle the head of the knee, and another servant to hang with the sick person, who encircles strongly the knee, for the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when the dislocation is at its farthest point, put the sick person in a lying position, as we have said in that of the hip-bone, and tie one cord on the healthy leg properly, and also on the thigh.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	then put two skewers, one at the head and the other at the feet, then stick one skewer between the knees of the sick person in the shape of an "X".

Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil. et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be in place when the sick person stretches out their legs and they will be even. Then bind the knees together, apply the poultice, and tie a bandage around it, so that the hip does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and if the sick person rests for three or four days, then remove the bandage and apply a poultice again. de la dislocation dou genoil	This is a continuation of the medieval medical text I was translating earlier.
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The joints are dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and do not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend their leg against their knee, and if it does not straighten at their knee, know that they are dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all this is that you have the patient sit up straight and stretch their leg if they can, and put your back against their face, and place their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take their knee to your palms and draw it between your two hands, then bend the two sides of the knee together; and another attendant stretches out their foot, as far as the joint comes back into its place, and the sign is that they straighten their leg slightly against their knee.

de la dislocation dou talon	It seems like you're switching to a different medical condition.

des dois	It seems like you want me to say something about the text being from the "Traité sur les maladies de la peau" by Guy de Chauliac (also known as De chirurgia), a medieval medical treatise, specifically the section on treating foot injuries or dislocations. Is that correct?

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	It seems like you're grouping together the sections from the medieval medical text that deal with both wounds and dislocations of the feet. This section appears to be part of a larger treatise on treating injuries, specifically those affecting the hands (dos) and feet.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with the dislocation, and you want to restore it, many times has happened that the sick person dies.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not confident in the treatment, since you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful, nor hasty.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and take at the beginning soothing things and apply hot compresses, and leave the sick person in God's hand, if you do not see hope for their recovery.

Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the Roman (or Romain) of Physic.
